Board met pursuant to law and pursuant to Resolution 06-R-09.

OFFICIAL RECORD
President Pro Tempore Moreno in the Chair.

At 10:00 A.M ., being the hour appointed for the meeting, the President Pro Tempore called the Board to
order.

BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY
PRESIDENT
LETTER OF RESIGNATION
Transmi tting a Communicati on, dated June 30, 2006 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR. , President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
To my colleagues, the Cook County Board of Commissioners, the hard working employees of Cook
County Government, and to all the people of Cook County, I must inform you that effective July 1, 2006,
I hereby tender my letter of resignation as the nominee for President of the Cook County Board. As of
July 31, 2006, I will retire as the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners and the Forest
Preserve District and as Commissioner of the 4th District of Cook County.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commi ssioner Butler, moved that the communication be received and
fil ed. The motion carried unanimously.

2

Use of Mobile Telephones
11-50

(a) Except as provided by subsection (b) of this section, no person shall drive a motor vehicle
while using a mobile cellular analog wireless or digital telephone.
(b) The provisions of this section shall not apply to:
(I) Law enforcement officers and operators of emergency vehicles when on duty and acting
in their official capacities;
(2) Persons using a telephone with a " hands free" device allowing the driver to talk into and
Iis ten to the other party without the use of hands;
(3) Persons using a telephone to call 911 telephone numbers or other emergency telephone
numbers to contact public safety forces;

(4) Person using a telephone while maintaining a motor vehic le in a stationary parked
position. and not in gear.

provided however. that if a violation occurs at the time of a traffic accident. the driver may be

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AN ORDINANCE DEALING WITH TEMPORARY OR PERMANENT ABSENCE
IN THE OFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government pursuant to the 1970 Illinois
Constitution, Article VII , Section 6(a); and

WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule power, the County of Cook may exercise any power and perfonn
any functi on relating to its government and affairs protecting health, safety and we lfare; and
WHEREAS, the 25th Amendment to the United States Constitution creates a process to address a
temporary, voluntary absence of the President of the United States; and
WHEREAS, Cook County , in order to properly manage its government and affairs, needs to address a
temporary, voluntary absence of the Office of the President of the Cook County Board; and
WHEREAS, to protect the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of Cook County and in order to
ensure that the government of Cook County has an Acting Executive with the duties and power of the
President if the elected President declares that he/she is temporarily unable to discharge the powers and
duties of the office; and
WHEREAS, if the President vacates the Office of the President for any reason an orderly succession
should be established in order to provide continuity in the Office of the President.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE
COMMISSIONERS, THAT:

IT

ORDAINED

11

BY

THE

COOK

COUNTY

BOARD OF

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

A.

Temporary Vacancy

Whenever the President transmits to the Board of Commissioners a written declaration that he/she is
temporarily unable to discharge the powers and duties of the office due to health or other reason; then the
Board shall select and appoint one of their number to serve as Acting President until the Pres ident
transmits a written declaration to the Board of Commissioners that he/she is able to discharge the powers
and duties of the Office of the President. The Acting President shall have all of the responsibilities,
power and duties to the Office of the President while serving as Acting President. The President shall
continue to receive the pay and benefits of the Office of the President during any such temporary absence.
B.

Permanent Vacancy

If the Office of the President becomes vacant for any reason causing the Board of Commissioners to
choose a successor until the next election, the succession line shall be as follows:
I.
Chairman of Finance - The person holding this position shall assume the Acting
President role no matter what political affiliation of said person or how many years of service as a County
Board member.
2.
Most Senior Commissioner - If the Chairman of Finance cannot assume the role of
Acting President, or desires not to assume that office, then the most Senior County Board member
currently holding office shall be named the Acting President by the remaining Commissioners.
3.
Years of Service - The senior member is defined as that member of the Board who has
the most combined years as an elected and/or appointed Cook County Commissioner whether the years
are continuous or staggered.

This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AN AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE OF 2001 TO ADD A
NEW SECTION PROHIBITING CERTAIN NEGATIVE USE RESTRICTIONS
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government pursuant to the 1970 111 inois
Constitution, Article VII, Section 6(a); and
WHEREAS, in accordance wi th Article VII, Section 6, and subject to the lim itations set forth therein, the
County of Cook may exercise any power and perform any function relating to its government and affairs;
and

12

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the County of Cook has passed a comprehensive zoning ordinance, known as the Cook
County Zoning Ordinance of 200 1 ("Ordinance") that is intended to promote the purposes set fo rth in
Article 2 of the Ordinance, including, without limitation, the public hea lth, safety , morals, comfort,
convenience and general welfare of the res idents of unincorporated Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that these purposes are furthered when property is used consistently
with the permitted and special uses identified in the Ordinance; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that the public health, safety and general welfare of the residents of
unincorporated Cook County are furthered when residents have access to grocery stores and drug stores,
both of which meet basic human needs; and
WHEREAS, Section 8. 1.2 of the Ordinance provides that the most restrictive regulation sha ll govern
when a requirement imposed by this Ordinance conflicts with any covenant or private agreement; and
WHEREAS, while the Ordinance recognizes the right of private parties to impose restrictions greater
than those set forth in the Ordinance, which will be recogni zed if they are valid and enforceable under
Illinois law, private parties are not free to enter into and impose restri ctions against private property if
such restrictions are against public policy ; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that Negative Use Restrictions, which enable a prior owner or
operator of a grocery store or drug store, after term inating operations at a site, to prevent any competitor
from operating a grocery store or drug store at such site in the future, limit uses that would otherwise be
permitted under the Ordinance; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that such Negative Use Restrictions are separate and distinct from
commercia lly reasonable non-compete clauses included in shopping center development agreements,
whereby a landlord may agree w ith a tenant that is a grocery store or drug store not to lease other space in
the same shopping center to a second grocery store or drug store in order to induce the tenant to sign a
long-term lease as an anchor tenant; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that such Negative Use Restrictions frustrate the purposes of the
Ordinance, serve no public purpose, compromi se the public health, safety, and general welfare, and
deprive the residents of unincorporated Cook County of the benefits of competition in the marketplace,
and cause significant deleterious and blighting effects on the affected comm un ity; and
WHEREAS, the County Board find s that the public health, safety, and general welfare of residents of
unincorporated Cook County are furthered when residents have access to grocery stores and drug stores,
both of w hi ch meet basic human needs; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds, in contrast, however, that Negative Use Restrictions, which enable
a prior owner or operator of a grocery store or drug store, after terminating operations at a site, to prevent
any competi tor from operating a grocery store at such site in the future serve no public purpose but
instead have significant deleterious and blighting effects on the affected comm unity's health, safety and
general welfare; and
WHEREAS, the County Board finds that because grocery stores and drug stores frequently occupy large
tracts of land in the center of residentia l neighborhoods or at key inte rsections, the continued presence of
grocery stores or drug stores in unincorporated Cook County serves as a catalyst to other economic
development and advances the health, safety and general welfare of the residents of that community,
particularly those who are elderly or economically disadvantaged.

13

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDING S FOR JULY 12, 2006

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Article 8
of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance of 2001 is amended by adding a new Section 8.1 .3 and changing
the numbering of the succeeding provisions as follows:
8.1.3

CERTAIN NEGATIVE USE RESTRICTIONS PROHIBITED AS AGAINST
PUBLIC POLICY

Notwithstanding Section 8. 1.2, a private agreement that purports to impose recorded negati ve use
restrictions upon real property in unincorporated Cook County so as to prohibit or have the
economic or practical effect of prohibiting the use of such real property for grocery store or drug
store purposes after a grocery store or drug store owner or operator of a store in excess of 7,500
square feet has terminated operations at the site, when such uses would otherwise be permitted,
including as a special use under this Ordinance, and which negative use restriction has a term of
more than one year, shall be against public policy, shall be void and unenforceable, and shall be
subject to remedial and enfo rcement powers under Sections 13. I 0 and 13. 11 of this Ordinance.
The foregoi ng prohibition shall not apply to an owner or operator of a grocery store or drug store
who terminates operations at a site for purposes of relocating such operations into a comparable
or larger store located within one-half mi le of the site where operations have term inated, provided
such relocation and the commencement of operations at the new site occurs within two years and
the negative use restriction imposed does not have a term in excess of three years. The Zoning
Administrator shall have discretion to extend the one-half mile lim it set forth in the preceding
sentence by one-half mi le ( i.e. to one mile) and to extend the two year commencement of
operations period by one year (i.e. to three years) upon the owner or operator's written request
and presentation of evidence establishing extenuating circumstances that establ ish good cause for
such extension(s). The requesting party shall also provide notice and a copy of such written
evidence to the district Commissioner(s) for the district in which the closed store and the new
store are located at the same time such submission is made to the Zoning Adm inistrator. The
foregoing prohibition shall apply regardless of whether the private agreement is incorporated in a
deed restriction, a restrictive covenant, T a lease or memorandum of lease, or any other recorded
instrument.
8.1.~ ~

ORDINANCE CONTENTS NOT A PERMIT

The contents of this Ordinance shall not be deemed a permit to use any property or to locate,
construct or maintain any building, structure or facility or to carry on any trade, industry,
occupation or activity.

8.1.4 ~ CUMULATIVE REGULATIO NS
The provisions of thi s Ordinance are cumulati ve with other laws and ordinances applying to the
same subject matters.

8.1.S ~ INDEX
The index appended to this Ordinance is solely a reference guide, and shall not be construed as
part of th is Ordinance.

This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J ULY 12, 2006

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Submitting a Proposed Ordi nance sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONA DO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
LARR Y SUFFREDIN, County Comm issioner
PRO POSED O RDI NANCE

WHEREAS, a nationwide and regional shortage of trained medica l professionals has threatened the
timely deli very of health services to patients in the Cook County Bureau of Health Services ("B ureau"),
an institution which the poor, the uninsured, and the underinsured solely re ly upon for their health care
needs; and
WHEREAS, this shortage of medical professionals including nurses, pharmacists, and radiology
technicians, combined with com petitive salary rates for these positions in the private sector, has created a
rapidly shrinking pool of specific healthcare personnel in the Bureau; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau's current policy of hiring outside agencies to compensate for the lack of fulltime professional staff, especially in the case of nurses, is a temporary solution that is costly and
unpredictable; and
WHEREAS, despite the fact that more than 40% of our patients are Latino, less than 3% of physicians,
5% of nurses, and 0% of phannacists are Latino. However, the Bureau has been unsuccessful in
recrui ti ng an adequate number of bilingual profess ionals who have the language skills and cultural
knowledge to address the health needs of our growing Latino patient base; and
WHEREAS, there are many students of Lati n American origin, some of whom are undocumented, who
live in Cook County and work towards profess ional degrees in schools throughout Illinois, as well as
Latin Amer ican healthcare professionals who live in Cook County and are seeking licensure to practice
their profession in Ill inois; and
W HEREAS, after receiving an excellent education in our schools, many of these Latin Ameri can
students are unable to find employment because of their immigration status and are forced to return to
their country of origin; and
WHEREAS, in Cook County a lone, there are hundreds of highly skilled Latin American students
studying in various healthcare fields who are ready, willing, and able to contribute their skills and talents
during this healthcare staffing crisis; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has establ is hed itself as an immigrant friendly county and, as such, should
take the lead in demonstrating the benefits of hiring highly skilled, foreign-born healthcare professiona ls
to a lleviate our staffing shortages and strengthen our public health system; and
WHEREAS, it is the responsibil ity of our public health system to provide adequate staffi ng to perform
vita l funct ions in the de li very of government services during a protracted nationwide and regional
shortage of essential licensed medical professionals.

15

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners shall enact
the following ordinance to establish a Foreign Healthcare Professional Pilot Program with the goal of
sponsoring twenty (20) bilingual Latino immigrants in identified areas of healthcare shortages in the
County.
SECTION 1. TITLE
This Ordinance shall be known and may be cited as the "Cook County Foreign Healthcare Professional
Pilot Program Ordinance."

SECTION 2. DEFINITIONS
For the purpose of this Ordinance, unless the context otherwise requires, the following words or terms
shall have the meanings respectively applied to them:
A. " Board" shall mean the Cook County Board of Comm issioners.
B. " Bureau" shall mean the Cook County Bureau of Health Services.
C. "County" shall mean County of Cook, State of Illinois.
D. " H-1 B visa" shall mean a visa used by a foreign worker who will be employed temporarily
on a nonimmigrant basis in a specialty occupation such as medicine and health.
E. "Latin American student" shall mean an individual born in a Central, South American or
Caribbean country, but who now resides and studies in Cook County .
F. " Latin American professional" shall mean a Latin American national from Central America,
South American, or the Caribbean, who received professional education in another country
and now, seeks to be licensed here in the United States.
G. " U.S. licensure" shall mean a license acquired after taking the required exams or fu lfilling
certain requirements in order to be able to practice professionally in the United States.

SECTION 3. PURPOSE OF PILOT PROGRAM
The Bureau wi ll work with the Latin American Consulates in Cook County to identi fy, train, sponsor and
employ Latin American individuals who are currently enrolled in college or seeking U.S. licensure and
desire to become healthcare professionals in the Bureau. By hiring undocumented graduates of our
educational system, or sponsoring the visa applications and hiring graduates and those seeking licensure
in the U.S., the County will ensure a pool of qualified, bilingual individuals to meet the ir healthcare
professional needs. In addition, these individuals of Latin American origin will also fill the special need
that the Bureau has for bilingual personnel.

SECTION 4. MEMORANDUM OF UNDERSTANDING
In order to faci litate the implementation of this Ordinance, the Board shall enter into a Memorandum of
Understanding with the Latin American Consulates in Cook County to provide assistance and guidance in
the selection process of program candidates. The Memorandum of Understanding becomes effective
thirty (30) days after passage of this Ordinance.

16

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

SECTION 5. SELECTION PROCESS OF PROGRAM CANDIDATES
A.

B.

Pursuant to the Memorandum of Understanding, the Bureau will provide the following
information on its healthcare professional needs to the Consulates:
I.

List of the healthcare positions that are vacant in the Bureau d ue to a s hortage of
professionals;

2.

Educational or licens ing requ irements for each position.

Purs uant to the Memorand um of Understanding, the Consulates will identify and
interview ten ( I 0) student and ten (I 0) professional candidates to determ ine the ir
e ligi bility for the program and wi ll provide the following in formation to the Bureau o n
selected candidates applying for the program:
I.

Proof that the candidate's principal place of residency is within Cook County ;

2.

Proof of citizenshi p from Latin American country of origin;

3.

For student candidates, verification of enrollment at a college or university in
Illinois and college transcripts;

4.

For professional candidates, re levant undergraduate and graduate degrees and
relevant healthcare certi ti cations; and

5.

All other relevant documentatio n as req uired by the Bureau.

C.

Upon receipt of the list of selected candidates from the Consulate, the Bureau will
conduct another round of interviews and any testing deemed necessary to veri fy the
acc uracy of the info rmation provided and to recommend candidates for the program.

D.

Final candidates shal l be selected by a Selection Panel comprised of the Bureau Chief,
the Cons ul Generals, and the Chief of the Bureau of Human Reso urces.

SECTION 6. COUNTY SPONSORSHIP OF SELECTED CANDIDATES
A. The County will sponsor the visa applications (H-1 B and other categories) of selected
candidates in the program and follow all necessary rules and procedures as set fo rth by the
U.S . Department of Labor Employment & Training Admini stration including, but not limited
to, the following requirements:
I. The County shall submit a completed Labor Conditio n Appl ication (LCA) in the
manner prescribed by the regulations;
2.

The County shall make the LCA and supporting documentation available for public
examination;

3.

The County shall s ubmit a copy of the approved LCA to U.S. C itizenship and
Immigration Services (USCIS) with a completed petition requesting H-1 B
classification;

17

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

4.

The County shall not allow the nonimmigrant worker to begin work until USCIS
grants the worker authorization;

5.

The County s ha ll ma intain documentation to meet its burden of proof with respect to
the validity of the statements made in its LCA and the accuracy of information
provided, in the event that such statement or information is challenged; and

6.

The County shall inform Cook County workers of the intent to hire a foreign worker
by posting the completed LCA for the position.

B. In those instances where a student or professional does not yet have the appropriate
documentation to work or study in the U.S. , the County would sponsor their visa application,
s ubject to a waiver of applicable federal law.

SECTION 7. SEVERABILITY
If any secti on, subsection, paragraph, sentence or clause of this Ordinance o r the appl ication thereof to
any person is fo r any reason deemed to be invalid or unconstitutional, such decis ion shall not affect,
impair or invalidate any remaining section, subsection, paragraph, sentence or clause hereof or the
application of this ordinance to any other person.

SECTION 8. EFFECTIVE DATE
This Ordinance shall take full force and effect immediate ly upon passage.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
ELI ZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, JOSEPH MAR IO MORENO,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA , MIKE QU IGLEY and DEBORAH SIMS, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

ESTABLISHING A JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER ADVISORY BOARD
WHEREAS, Cook County is authorized by the State of Illinois to operate a juvenile temporary detentio n
center for the custody and care of minors, under the age of 17, while awaiting trial ; and
WHEREAS, the facility is a detention center, it operates a school and inherently includes recreation and
housing facilities; and
WHEREAS, Cook County expends $25 million in operating this facility on an annual basis; and

18

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the center is the subject of a lawsuit and consent decree in the United States District Court
alleging improprieties in its operation and the handling of minors; and
WHEREAS, it is deemed to be in the public interest to operate the center in the most commendable,
humanitarian, and efficient manner; and
WHEREAS, it is deemed to be in the public interest to solicit and accept opinions, advice and
counsel from professionals in the greater Cook County community; and
WHEREAS, such professional opinions, advice and counsel, should be accepted in order to formu late
policy for the proper administration of the facility, in terms of juvenile detention, short term education of
minors awaiting trial, and to create as positive an atmosphere as possible for these minors.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners:
1) authori ze and direct the creation of an I I member Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention
Center Community Advisory Board, consisting of at least one representative of each of the following
professions : juveni le detention and corrections professionals, educators, attorneys, social workers,
medical professionals and other members of the community interested in the appropriate care of
minors, no later than October I, 2006, with such appointments made by the President upon the advice
and consent of the Board of Commissioners, for tenns of two years; and
2) grant such board the power and responsibil ity of reviewing the policies and practices related to the
adm inistration of the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
3) require that such counsel and advice be provided to the Juven ile Temporary Detention Center's
administration, to the President and Board of Commissioners as appropriate and to provide an annual
report to the President and Board of Commissioners or the appropriate committee; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such counsel shall be advisory, and subject to the authority of the
President and Board of Commissioners.
Commiss ioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Goslin, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Family Court and Ju venile Detention Center Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 28025 1). The
motion carried unanimously.

requesting authorization to extend the current funding cycle for 90 days from July I , 2006 to September

President' s Office of Employment and Training (POET). The original authorization to fund the program
was given on September 8, 2005 by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

The extension is necessary in order to accommodate funding schedules established by the lllinois
Department of Commerce and Economic Opportunity and to synchronize the County 's contract cycle
with the federal fiscal year.
POET has redesigned a portion of the 2006-2007 program to provide specific fundi ng fo r targeted
populations that have more barriers to employment including individuals with limited English
proficiency; individual s seeking re-entry into society and out-of-sc hool youth in economically
disadvantaged areas. Additional dollars will be targeted to occupations in growth ind ustries located in
Cook County, including healthcare, transportation/logistics/warehousing, information technology and
others identified th rough the Cook County Workforce Investment Board, a public/private partnership.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. There are sufficient funds available in the grant to accommodate this
request.

OFFICE OF THE CLERK OF THE CIRCUIT COURT
AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 22, 2006 from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a managed service agreement with
BearingPoint, Inc., Austin, Texas, to implement the approved Electronic Filing Pilot Program for
commercial litigation cases in the Law Division. This pilot project was approved by the Illinois Supreme
Court at its May 2006 term.
On June 14, 2006, the Administrative Office of Illinois Courts informed me and the Honorable Timothy
C. Evans, Chief Judge, of the Supreme Court's action. A copy of the June 14, 2006 letter has been
submitted.
Pursuant to the Illinois Supreme Court's "Policy for Implementation of an Electronic Filing Pilot Project
for lllinois' Courts", the Clerk of the Circuit Court released a request for information (" RFI") on April 23 ,
2004 and so licited responses to more than fifteen ( 15) companies. The request for information (" RFI")
was sent to a ll companies as well as an instruction letter posted on the internet on the Clerk of the C ircuit
Court's website.
Five (5) firms s ubmitted responses to the request for information (" RFI" ) produced by the C lerk of the
Circuit Court. BearingPoint, Inc. was selected after completion of an extensive review of all proposal s
and was deemed the company most able to fulfill the requirements of the Clerk of the C ircuit Court.
BearingPoint, Inc. is the so le electronic filing vendor capable of providing an electronic filing system
capable of meeting the requirements set forth in the approved e lectronic filing app lication. Specifically,
Bearing Point, Inc. is the only vendor capable of providing an " open" electronic filing system that
provides e lectronic fil ers with a choice of electronic filing service providers while providing the C lerk ' s
Office with a single review queue interface for clerk and court employees.
The anticipated implementation of this two (2) year pilot program wi ll begin in early fall 2006. This
program will allow attorney 's and se lf-represented litigants to s ubmit court documents electronically fo r a
convenience fee of $4.00 and to serve those documents electronically for a convenience fee of $2 .00 paid
to BearingPoint, Inc. All applicable statutory filing fees will be remitted to the Clerk of the Circuit Court
with the electronic filing on a regular basis with no financ ial impact to Cook County.
Estimated Fi scal Impact: None.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested agreement. The motion carried unanimously.

33

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Reason:

The Election Department is renewing these contracts because the current vendors are now
familiar with the special attention requ ired to safely and securely transport the new election
equipment, as well as the new and much larger voting supply carriers, to more than 1,300
polling locations all across suburban Cook County. Additionally, j ust months after the
November 7, 2006 general e lection, the county election division must conduct the 2007
suburban municipal e lections (February 27 and April 17). The April 17, 2007 consolidated
munic ipal election is generall y considered to be one of the country's most complex elections
in terms of the number of candidates, election jurisdictions and ballot styles. For these
reasons, the Election Department believes it is necessary to seek a renewal of the current
contract in order to insure the successful completion of thi s critical election division
responsibility.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $2, 129,4 71.00 ($ 1,064, 735.50 per year). Contract period: December I, 2006
through November 30, 2008. (524-430 Account). Requisition Nos. 7524000 I, 75240002 and 75240003.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2007 and fu ture year funds.
Commiss ioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to renew the requested contracts. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 26, 2006 from
DAVID ORR, County Clerk
by
CLEM BALANOFF, Director of Elections
The Election Department has combined 32 precincts in suburban Cook County into 16. The precincts
were housed in the same locations, so that voters will sti ll go to the same place to vote. This wi ll make
them more equal in size and save the taxpayers money. Maps of those townships that have changed in the
precinct boundaries as well as the street index files (pull keys) for the addresses and streets of the newly
drawn precincts have been submitted.

PROPOSED CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., C hief, Bureau of Health Services
and
CATHERINE MARAS O'LEARY, Chief Information Officer,
Bureau of Information Teclmology and Automation
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with ACS Healthcare Solutions,
Dearborn, Michigan, for infonnation technology (IT) services for the Bureau of Health Services (BHS).

40

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Reason:

Through a request for proposal process ACS Healthcare Solutions had the lowest cost
proposal and met all County requi rements. This proposed contract will provide staff
augmentation services to meet the technology needs of the data center, help desktop,
application support, network, and packaged rollout and application development (PRAD)
towers and improve the IT service delivery model through standardization, the creation of
service level agreements and better coordination with the County's Bureau of Information
Technology and Automation. Moreover, the base cost of this proposal minus the additional
monies included for PRAD services is approximately 42 percent lower than the current
provider. ACS will complete the installation of BHS-owned appl ications, including the
Cemer system, and will supplement the staff that is currently identified in this proposal at
peak times at no additional cost to the County. For the revenue cycle, ACS will assess and
remedy any issues relating to the Cerner/S iemens interface as an additional comm itment to
the County. Accordingly, ACS has met the County's MBE/WBE requirement.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $14,607, 122.00 (Year I: $4,807, 122.00; Year 2 : $4,850,000.00; and Year 3:
$4,950,000.00). Contract period: January I, 2007 through December 31, 20 I 0. (897-260 Account).
Requisition No. 78970014.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2007 and futu re year funds.

Note: This item also appears under the Bureau of Information Technology and Automation.
Com missioner Si lvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the communication be referred
to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 280247). The motion carried unanimously.

06-R-275
RESOLUTION
RESOLVED, by the Members of the Board of Comm issioners of Cook County, Illinois, on behalfofthe
County of Cook, to authorize and direct its President to execute, by original signature or his authorized
signature stamp, two (2) copies of a Letter of Agreement between the County of Cook and the County of
Lake, submitted, wherei n the County of Lake will conduct an intersection improvement feasibility study
to define a locally preferred intersection design a lternative for future improvements to the intersection of
Lake-Cook Road (County Hig hway A50) at Arlington Heights Road (County Hig hway Y69), said study
to include data collection (previous studies, roadway plans, util ities, right-of-way), traffic projections and
capacity ana lyses, alternate intersection geometric studies, traffic simulations, construction cost estimates,
local agency coordination and project administration ; the County of Cook wi ll pay seventy-five percent
(75%) of the engineering costs for the study (Cook County share of costs not to exceed $22,500 .00) under
County Section: 06-ASO 13-0 I -ES; and, the Highway Department is authori zed and directed to forward
two (2) executed copies of this Agreement with certified copies of this Resolution to the County of Lake
for further processing.
July 12, 2006

BUREAU OF INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY AND AUTOMATION
PROPOSED CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DANIEL H. WINSHIP, M.D., Chief, Bureau of Health Services
and
CATHERINE MARAS O' LEARY, Chief lnfonnation Officer,
Bureau oflnfonnation Technology and Automation
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with ACS Healthcare Solutions,
Dearborn, Michigan, for information technology (IT) services for the Bureau of Health Services (BHS).
Reason:

Through a request for proposal process ACS Healthcare Solutions had the lowest cost
proposal and met all County requirements. This proposed contract will provide staff
augmentation services to meet the technology needs of the data center, help desktop,
application support, network, and packaged rollout and appl ication development (PRAD)
towers and improve the IT service delivery model through standardization, the creation of
service level agreements and better coordination with the County's Bureau of lnfonnation
Technology and Automation. Moreover, the base cost of this proposal minus the additional
monies included for PRAD services is approximately 42 percent lower than the current
provider. ACS will complete the installation of BHS-owned applications, including the
Cerner system, and will supplement the staff that is currently identified in this proposal at
peak times at no additional cost to the County. For the revenue cycle, ACS will assess and
remedy any issues relating to the Cerner/Siemens interface as an additional commitment to
the County. Accordingly, ACS has met the County's MBE/ WBE requirement.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $14,607, 122.00 (Year I: $4,807,122.00; Year 2: $4,850,000.00; and Year 3:
$4,950,000.00). Contract period: January I, 2007 through December 31, 20 I 0. (897-260 Account).
Requisition No. 78970014.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2007 and future year funds.

Note: This item also appears under the Bureau of Health Services.

referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 280247). The motion carried
unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE CHIEF JUDGE
GRANT APPLICATION
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 5, 2006 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization to apply for a grant in the amount of $200,000.00 from the U.S. Department of
Justice, Office of Justice Programs. This grant would expand funding for gender-responsive treatment
services to felony offenders that have significant menta l illness and substance abuse disorders who are
referred to the court' s Mental Health Treatment Court.
In April 2004, the Circuit Court of Cook County launched the Mental Health Treatment Court pilot
program in the Criminal Division to enhance court supervision of mentally ill offenders by improving the
delivery of mental health care. The ultimate goal of the program is to reduce incarceration of mentally ill,
non-violent felony offenders. In its first two years of operation, the program has received 95 referrals and
has 36 active participants, both male and female. Most participants have substance abuse disorders in
add ition to chronic mental illness and other health concerns, such a positive tests for HIV. Early program
results are encouraging, as recidivism for participants has been substantially reduced. The grant fund s
wi ll be used to increase the participant capacity of the program by an additional 25 offenders, or 75 per
year.
The grant requires no cash matching funds and as such, would have no fiscal impact on the county.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item , and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None.
through October 3 I, 2008.

Grant Award:

$200,000.00.

Funding period:

November I, 2006

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Chief
Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

GRANT AWARD ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated .lune 9, 2006 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization to accept a supplemental grant award in the amount of $200,000.00 and extend
for one ( I) year grant funding from the Annie E. Casey Foundation for the court's Juvenile Detention
Alternative Initiatives (JDA I) model site activities.
Since 1998, the foundation recognized the Circuit Court of Cook County as a national model site for
juvenile detention reform. As a national model site, the court hosts delegations from jurisdictions around
the country who visit Cook County to study the court' s juvenile detention reform efforts. The majority of
this funding is used to reimburse the court for expenses incurred in fulfilling its model site duties. The
grant a lso funds a director of research retained on a contractual basis, training, supplies, and publications
for JDAI programming.

CONTRACT RENEW AL

Transmitting a Communication from
MARY JO HORACE, Director, Department of Office Technology
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 06-41-292 with NTT/Verio,
Chicago, Illinois, for unlimited secure Internet access via dedicated circuit connections and web hosting
services through Cook County's wide area network.
Reason:

The contract will provide Cook County uninterrupted access to the Internet via the county's
wide area network and have secure web hosting services. The increase is needed to allow

PROPOSED CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
JOHN A. FAIRMAN, SR., Chief Operating Officer, Provident Hospital of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Automed Technologies,
Inc., Vernon Hills, ll linois, for the purchase of a pharmacy automation system.
Reason:

Automed Technologies, Inc. is the manufacturer and only authorized source for the Optifill II
pharmacy automation system. The Optifill II is the only system that provides automated
capping for robotically filled oral solid medications, automated patient order collection,
automated patient order routing, automated order initiation, image capture of all robotically
filled prescriptions for comparison to reference images, and the ability for operators to
overwrite, or create new reference images. This system has the abil ity to process up to 200
automatically filled bottles per hour, and an overall system capacity of up to 1,800
prescriptions per shift.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $766,350.00. One time purchase. (717/891-579 Account). Req uisition No.
68910543.
Sufficient fund s have been appropriated to cover this request.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

neighborhoods within Cook County.

set forth in Cook County 05-0-18 (an amendment to an Ordinance Establi shing, and approv ing the
increase of, rental charges for the lease of Cook County real estate tax data by commercial users and noncommercial users), approved by the Board on March 15, 2005 which governs the leasing and use of
certain real estate tax data.

amended Ordinance.

Transmitting a Communication from
MICHAEL F. SHEA HAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
TIMOTHY BRENNAN, Director of Vehicle Services
requesting authorization for the Purchas ing Agent to advertise for bids for the purchase of twenty-five
(25) Federal S ignal lightbar packages and twenty-five (25) Setina prisoner screens/partitions for Ford
Crown Victoria police automobiles.
Reason:

The Sheriff's Department vehicles for the last four (4) years have used the Federal Signal
product. By using Federal Signal as a sole product provider, Vehicle Services will be able to
order parts when needed and keep the uniformity of the electrical equipment with one
company. Interchanging lightbars and equipment from various manufacturers would be costly
and could cause problems within the lightbar packages. These items can be bid through vari ous
vendors.

One time purchase. (7 17/211-550 Account). Requisition No. 621 10515.
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
The Vehicle Steering Committee concurs w ith this recommendation.

DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State' s Attorney' s Office
requesting authorization to apply for a grant in the amount of $250,000.00 from the U.S. Department of
Justice, Bureau of Justice Assistance, for the State' s Attorney's new Misdemeanor Mental Health
Diversion Program. If awarded, the grant will provide thirty (30) months of funding for the purpose of
referring mentally ill, non-violent, misdemeanor offenders to a diversion program and link them to
community-based mental health treatment as an alternative to prosecution.
This grant requires that the office match 20 percent of the grant award. The match commitment for this
program is an in-kind match that suppo1ts I 0 percent of the salary and fringe benefits of the program
coordinator. Additional in-kind match funding will be provided by program partner agencies, T ASC and
Heartland Alliance.

the coronary artery stent that is visible under tluoroscopy which assures accurate placement.

re-stenos is (closure) of the artery.

ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WIRELESS TELECOMMUNICATIONS ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY
AS AMENDED (01-0-32, 02-0-24)
ARTICLE 1
WIRELESS TELECOMMUNICATION FACILITIES
1.0

PURPOSE
Provisions of this Ordinance are intended to address public safety concerns, promote aesthetic
values and provide appropriate locations for wireless telecommunication facilities. This
Ordinance establishes minimum standards for the location, installation, height and
landscaping of wireless telecommunication facilities and encourages co-location of multiple
service providers.

1.1

PERMITS FOR WIRELESS TELECOMMUNICATION FACILITIES

1.1.1

PERMIT REQUIREMENTS
A pennit issued by the Department of Building and Zoning is required for all wireless
telecommunications facilities and related accessory structures. No new or existing wireless
telecommunications facility or accessory structure shall be erected altered or relocated
without first obtaining a permit.

1.1.2

PERMIT APPLICATION PROCEDURES
A.

B.

C.

Applications for wireless telecommunication facility permits shall be made to the
Department of Building and Zoning on forms furnished by the Department. All
applications shall be accompanied by a fee as established by the Cook County Board
of Commissioners.
Applications shall include information required to assure compliance with
regulations for wireless telecommunication facilities and with all other applicable
ordinances and regulations of Cook County .
Applicants shall provide a bond, in a form acceptable to the Department of Building
and Zoning, to insure that wireless telecommunication facilities will be constructed,
maintained and removed in accordance with thi s Ordinance.

135

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

D.

E.

1.1.3

Applicants shall submit an agreement to remove all facilities, structures and
driveways if the facility becomes technologically obsolete or ceases to perform its
original functi on for six (6) o r more consecutive mo nths. Upon removal, the
applicant shall restore the site to its original condition, less normal wear and tear and
seed all exposed soil.
Wireless telecommunicati on faci lity permits shall be issued by the Commi ssioner of
Building and Zoning if the facility complies with the provisions of this Ordinance
and with all other applicable ordinances and regulations of Cook County. Any
permit may be revoked at any time by the Department of Building and Zoning upon a
finding that a wireless te lecommunication facility violates any provision of this
Ordinance, of any other applicable Cook County O rd inance o r when a permit holder
has made fal se representations in securing a w ire less telecommunication facility
permit.

GENERAL REQUIREMENTS
A.
Wireless telecommunication facility is defi ned in Article 14 of the Cook County
Zoning Ordinance of 200 I under " telecomm unications carrier wi reless
communication transmitting and receiving facility". The terms "structure" and
" building" as used in this Ordinance are defined in Article 14 of the Cook County
Zoning Ordinance of 200 I. The term " public utility structure" as used in this
Ordinance is defined in the Illinois Compiled Statutes 220 ILCS 5/3- 105 inc ludes
electrical transm issio n and antenna towers, electrical power structures, and water
towers owned by municipalities, townships, speci al service districts, county or state
governments. "Cook County structure" includes any structure tower or building
owned or operated by Cook County or any of its agents, departments, licensees or
agencies.
B.
Co-location of a new wireless telecommunication facility on an existing rooftopi
public utility structure, Cook Co1:1Aty strnct1:1re or other existing structure shall not
exceed fifteen ( 15) feet above the highest point of the existing structure.

SPECIAL PROVISIONS
The following special provisions apply to wireless telecommunication facilities.
A.
Wireless telecommunication facilities and related accessory structures may be located
on zoning lots utilized for another use or improved with other structures or on zoning
lots where no principal use or structure exists.

137

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006
B.
C.
D.

E.

F.

G.

H.

Minimum lot area, lot width and fl oor area ratio regulations are inapplicable to
wireless telecommunication facilities and related accessory structures.
One off-street parking space shall be provided on site for each full-time employee
based upon the maximum number of employees per shift.
Ground, roof and pole mounted antennas shall be screened by fencing, buildings or
parapets that appear to be an integral part of the building or landscaping so that no
more than twenty-five (25) percent of the combined tower structure and antenna
height is visible from grade level of adjoining single-family zoned property. GeloeatioA of a Rew wireless teleeommtÂ·mieatioA f'aeility OA aA e>ti stiAg fH::1alie lcltiliD'

Wireless telecommunication fac il ity locations which abut a street, single-family
residence district or areas with public access, such as forest preserves, shall contain a
landscape buffer along the property line consisting of at least one row of coniferous
shrubs spaced not more than three (3) feet on center. Plant materials shall be of a
variety that will grow to at least five (5) feet in height within two (2) years. Geloeation of a Rew â¢.viFeless teleeommlinieation faeilitv OA an eKistiAg p1:1blie 1:1tiliD'

Applicants shall preserve existing vegetation on a proposed wireless
telecommunication facility site to the greatest extent possible and shall not remove
any trees exceeding four (4) inches diameter either prior or subsequent to the
issuance of a permit. Applicants shall submit a landscaping plan to the Department of
Building and Zoning for the removal of trees exceeding four (4) inches in diameter.
Wireless telecommunication facilities shall be either a galvanized fini sh or painted
gray above the surrounding treeline and painted green, black or sim ilar color below
the existing or landscaped tree line to blend into the natural surroundings.
Wireless telecommunication fac ilities, including anchor posts and supporting wires,
and all necessary structures, shall be completely surrounded by fencing at least six (6)
feet in height. The fence shall contain a locked gate at the junction of the access way
and a public thoroughfare.

1.4

CONDITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS
The Zoning Board of Appeals may recommend to the Board of Comm issioners such
conditions and restrictions upon the premises benefited by a variation as may be necessary to
reduce or minimize the effect of the variation upon other properties in the neighborhood and
to better carry out the general intent of this Ord inance. (Amend. Ord. 02-0-24, 07-09-02)

1.5

ACTION BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
A.
Final action shall not be taken by the Cook County Board of Commissioners on an
application for a variation until the Zoning Board of Appeals' findings of fact and
recommendations have been received.
B.
Variations in e>(eess of ten ( 10) pereent shall be passed by a favorable vote of three
quarters (3/4) of all Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners in cases
where the Zoning Board of Appeals has not recommended the variation.
C.
Applications for variations shall be deemed denied if the Cook County Board of
Com missioners has not taken fi nal action' within sixty (60) days of receiving the
Zoning Board of Appeals' findings and recommendations. The sixty (60) day period
may be extended if a request for an extension is made by the applicant or by a Cook
County Board Commissioner.
D.
The Cook County Board of Commissioners may impose conditions and restrictions
upon a variation in order to assure that the public health, safety and welfare is
adequately protected. (Amend. Ord. 02-0-24, 07-09-02)

138

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

1.6

ENFORCEMENT OF ORDINANCE
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning is responsible fo r enforcement of th is Ordinance.
A person, firm or corporation, and their agents, employees or contractors who violate,
disobey or refuse to comply with any provision of this Ordinance shall be subject to fines,
penalties and inj uncti ve relief as provided in Article I 3 of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance of 200 I.

of the height was discovered. It was requested by both Interrail and the owner's of the right-of-way that
the signs be removed. It was di scovered that lnterrail and the owner's of the right-of-way required a
variation which was forwarded to the Zoning Board of Appeals for a recommendation. The Zoning Board
of Appeals presented a recommendation for approval of variances for existing s igns to the Zoning and
Building Committee. The application was presented to the Zoning and Building Committee and the
variation was denied on June 6, 2006.
Chairman Silvestri requested Mr. Wlodarski to provide the Commissioners wi th additional information
pertaining to Communication Nos. 279299, 279300 and 279301 from the Illinois Department of
Transportation.
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to approve Communication Nos.
279299, 279300 and 279301, contingent upon approval by the Illinois Department of
T ransportation. The motion carried.

PRO POSED ORDI NANCE AMENDMENT
Amendment to the C ook C ounty Zoning Ordinance of2001 (01-0-30)
to include the G arage Sale Ordinance
WHE REAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit pursuant to Article VII , Section 6 of the
1970 Illinois Constitution; and
WHE REAS, as a home rule unit, Cook County may exercise any power and perform any
function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHE REAS, at this ti me there is no ordinance governing garage sales currently in the Cook
County Zoning Ordinance.
NOW, THE REFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Board of Commiss ioners
shall amend Article 4.1.5 R- 1 Sing le Family Residence District, Temporary Uses, of the
Cook County Zoning Ordinance to include Garage Sales as foll ows:

2,.

Garage Sales.
Garage sales shall be limited to two sales per household per year. Garage sales
shall be held for no more than 3 consecutive days. Garage sales shall only be
permitted between the hours of 8 a.m. and 6 p.m.

~

Other temporary uses as permitted by this Ordinance.

6.

T his Ordi nance shall be in effect immediately upon passage.
*Referred to the Committee on Zoning and Building 06/03/03.

140

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J ULY 12, 2006

Commissioner Gosl in stated that his concern is individual's operating a fl ea market sale out of their
garage sales.
Chairman Si lvestri asked the Building and Zoning Department if they have a mechanism to issue permits
for garage sa les and appropriate fee for garage sales permits.
Mr. Wlodarski replied the applicants would have to come downtown to obtain a permit. The Building
and Zoning Department does not have full-time staff at the court houses.
Chairman Silvestri suggested that the Building and Zoning Department do more extensive research on the
issues of permits fo r garage sales, working with townships and the Sheriffs Office.
Mr. Wlodarski stated most municipalities issue permits for garage sales. The Building and Zoning
Department would find it difficult enforcing the ordinance in judging household items as a garage sale.
There are no overtime funds available for weekend inspections of garage sale items.

Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to approve Communication No.
259637. The motion carried.
Vice Chairman Steele voted present and Commissioners Collins, Murphy and Sims voted no.

279320

COOK COUNTY JUVEN ILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER ST ATUS
(PROPOSED R ESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Earlean
Collins, County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by Jerry Butler, Forrest C laypool, John P.
Daley, Elizabeth Ann Doody Gorman, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Joseph Mario Moreno,
Joan Patricia Murphy, Anthony J. Peraica, Mike Quigley, Peter N. Silvestri , Deborah Sims,
Bobbie L. Steele and Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

COOK COUNTY JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER ST ATVS
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule un it of local government purs uant to Article VII
Section 6(a) of the I 970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exerci se any power and
perform any functi on pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, Cook County government has the responsibility for funding, operating and
monitoring the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and

150

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety
and welfare of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on juvenile
detention; and
WHEREAS, over the past several years there has been increasing all egations in reference to
the treatment of children, the qua lity of staff, management and operating procedures which
has resulted in litigation; and

WHEREAS, the parties to litigation have been in talks to resolve the concerns over the
Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Federal Court approved an Agreed S upplemental Order between the
litigants; and

WHEREAS, 1t is essential that the Board review and ascertain the fiscal impact of
implementation of the May 2006 Agreed Supplemental Order on the FY07 budget; and

WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Board review the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement,
the Juvenile Detention Alternative Initiative (JDAI) Self-Assessment Report, the
Implementation Plan, legal fees, and the progress made towards implementing the
requirements as set forth in the May 2006 Agreed Supplemental Order, the 2002
Memorandum of Agreement and the recommendations as set forth in the JDAI Se lfAssessment Report, the Annie E. Casey Foundation Report and the John Howard Association
Report.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this Board conduct a public hearing in
which the above mentioned documents and issues are reviewed and addressed.
Note:

This item was also refer red to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center
Subcommittee. (See Comm. No. 279319).

RESOLUTION REQUESTING A REVIEW OF ALL GRANTS AND GRANT FUNDED

(PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Earlean
Collins, County Commissioner.

152

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

REVIEW OF ALL GRANTS AND GRANT FUNDED PROGRAMS FOR
JUVENILE DELINQUENCY PREVENTION IN COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII
Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and
perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety
and welfare of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on juvenile
delinquency prevention; and
WHEREAS, it is essential that the Cook County Board of Comm issioners review all grants
and grant funded programs, including but not limited to, programs for juvenile offenders,
crime prevention, socia l services and s upportive services, involving juvenile delinquency
prevention; and
WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Cook County Board of Commissioners review all
agencies awarded grants for juvenile delinquency prevention programs, accountabil ity
measures and performance data.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
conduct a review of all grants and grant funded programs for juvenile delinquency prevention
and intervention to ascertain the fiscal and service impact in Cook County.
Note:

This item was also referred to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center
Subcommittee (See Comm. No. 279322).

*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/06/2006.
The Chairman asked ifthere were any questions on the proposed resolution. Hearing none, and having no
discussion, the Chairman entertai ned a motion to receive and file the above item .

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to receive and file
Communication No. 279323. The motion carried.
Commissioner Maldonado moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moreno.
The motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,
COMM ITTEE ON FINANCE
JOHN P. DALEY, Chairman
ATTEST : MICHELLE HARRIS, Secretary

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved that the Report of the Committee on
Finance ( Public Hearing) be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Commissioner Quigley inquired whether Ms. Dunnings is confident that the shortfalls that were discussed
in the prior meeting will be overcome this year.
Ms. Dunnings referenced a series of contracts approved at the June 20, 2006 Board meeting submitted by
the Bureau of Health Services. She further stated the Bureau of Health Services has broadened its
revenue enhancement initiative; they are aggressively pursuing the recovery of Supplemental Security
Income/Social Security Di sability Income funds. Additional ly, in April 2006 the Board approved a
resolution, which provides for the issuance of a monthly revenue report. In compliance with this
resolution, the commissioners are receiving a monthly update of these activities.

Commiss ioner Quigley inquired as to what the Bureau's shortfall was last year.
Walter K. Knorr, County Comptroller, replied the shortfall was $60 million in patient fees. There was an
additional IGT (Intergovernmental Transfer) payment, and the net shortfall was $40 million. He
concluded by stating the Bureau of Health Services spent I 00% of their budget last year.
Chairman Daley stated that he had subm itted a letter to a ll of the elected officials and department heads,
wherein he requested that the commissioners take up at the next Board Meeting the issue of holding
everyone to 96% of their appropriated funds. He requested that these parties reply to the letter today or
before the next board meeting.
Vice Chairman Steele voiced concern that Cook County vendors not be sacrificed in this reserving
process.
Chairman Daley repl ied that th is would not occur, and that contractual obligations would not be affected.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether any of the funds could be used in the 2007 Budget.
Thomas J. G laser, Chief Financial Officer, Bureau of Finance, replied in the negative. Mr. Glaser further
stated that the accrued s urplus in the 110 Account (Salaries & Wages of Regu lar Employees) is as of the
first pay period in June.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's inquiry, Ms. Dunnings stated that the amount of transfers under
$25,000 totals $225,538; the amount of transfers over $25,000, totals $23,871 ,278. She further stated that
these figures would be provided to the Board for the 2007 Transfer of Funds meeting.
Ms. Dunnings replied that various departments have ass ured her that these funds wi ll cover budgetary
needs until commencement of fiscal year 2007.
In response to Commissioner Goslin's question regarding the budget process, Ms. Dunnings responded
the budget is not a zero-based budget; each new budget is developed using the previous year's budget as a
guide.
Chairman Daley clarified the fiscal year began December I, 2005, and that this transfer of funds meeting
is based on the previous seven months of the c urrent fiscal year.
Commissioner Peraica made various mid-year transfer observations. He continued by stating since 2002,
the overall budget has grown; however the percentage of transfers has declined. The dec li ne in the
amount of transfers is a result of the commissioners restraining departments.

Commissioner C laypool asked Dr. Winship to expla in the purpose of the large transfer amounts into
overtime.
Dr. Daniel H. Winship, Chief, Bureau of Health Services, replied that the majority of the funds are being
allocated to nursing, phannacy, and laboratory and technology technician positions. These positions are
difficult to fill because of the market competition and the wages being offered by the Bureau of Health
Services. Dr. Winship further stated collective bargaining agreements also impact the need for this
transfer.
Commissioner Quigley inquired what overtime reduction measures are being pursued.
Dr. Winship replied that the Bureau of Health Services has an overtime reduction plan, wh ich is reviewed
at least monthly by the Chief Operating Officers and the Chief Medical Officers.
Chairman Daley announced that Jonathan Rothstein will be meeting with the commissioners individually
to discuss the status of the collective bargaining agreement currently being negotiated.
Commissioner Quigley inquired whether a collective bargaining agreement would necessitate further
transfers of funds.
Ms. Dunnings replied in the negative.
Commissioner Collins inqui red as to the amount of funds the Bureau of Health Services is allocating to
agencies that provide temporary employees.
Dr. Winship rep lied that the amount is approximately $400,000.
Commissioner Peraica inquired of John Clark, Chief Financial Officer, Cermak Health Services of Cook
County, whether the amount being transferred will be sufficient through the end of the fi scal year.
Mr. Clark replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Peraica inquired as to the number and nature of vacancies.
Mr. Clark replied that Cermak Health Services of Cook County currently has approximately 45 vacancies,
namely nurses, radiology technicians, etc.

158

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Ms. Dunnings provided the following c larification that the funds being transferred out of the I I 0 account
are earned surplus (budgeted pay from the vacancies not otherwise being utilized) through the first pay
period in June.
Mr. Clark specified that the recent Joint Comm ission on Accreditation of Healthcare Organizations
(JCAHO) accreditation required overtime work; and that Cermak Health Services of Cook County
currently has fifty-five vacant positions, including part-time vacancies.
Commissioner Peraica inquired as to the demand for health services at Cermak.
Mr. Clark replied that the sickness acuity level has risen; on average three hundred patients go through
intake daily. Those who are treatable remain; the others are transferred to Stroger Hospital of Cook
County or Provident Hospital of Cook County. Ten to sixteen dialysis patients are at Cermak at any
given time.
Mr. Clark replied that the overtime was spent in the Medical Records department, where staffing is
limited. Also, Cermak is not reimbursed when it provides photocopying for medical records requested by
the courts and the State ' s Attorney's Office.
Ms. Dunnings presented the following clarification regarding the term, "administrator", as shown on page
1-9 of the Budget Book. The budget is divided into business units. One of these business units is entitled,
"Admini stration." This unit includes administrative positions, as well as support positions for those
administrative positions.
In response to Commissioner Sims' concern regarding the use of overtime by the Bureau of Health
Services, Dr. Wi nship noted that the Bureau has substantially lowered its use, from $55 million in 2004,
to $46 million in 2005 and, for the first seven months in this year, only $20 million.
In response to Commissioner Peraica's inquiry, Sidney A. Thomas, Acting Chief Operating Officer,
Ambulatory and Community Health Network of Cook County (ACHN), stated that pharmacy and
radiology were transferred to Stroger Hospital of Cook County in the 2005 Budget. ACHN no longer
manages the outpatient pharmacy or radiology services .
Commissioner Quigley inquired as to the DuSable and Austin High School clinics.
Mr. Thomas replied that these clinics wi ll now be serving a larger population of four schools each.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the percentage allocations for the fi ve suburban c linics will
remain the same into the 2007 fi scal year, and whether these clinics wi ll continue to provide the same
level of service.
Mr. Thomas replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether any cuts are planned.
Mr. Thomas replied in the negative.
Commissioner Peraica inquired what the purpose is for the transfer of $920,563 in funds from Budgetary
Unit 898.

159

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Dr. Winship replied that this is the same type of transfer as the one Mr. C lark described.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how many vacancies the Bureau of Health Services currently has.
Dr. Winship replied that the Bureau of Health Services currently has approximately 600 vacancies.
Commissioner Peraica inquired why the transfer rate into Account 260 has risen from $400,000 in 2005
to $2,320,000 in 2006.
Dr. Winship replied that this is due to the growth of the mail order pharmacy. The total transfer fo r the
year will be $7,300,000 and this will provide enough funding until fiscal year 2007.
Com missioner Peraica inquired as to the need for the transfer from Provident Hospital of Cook County.
John A. Fairman, Sr., Chief Operating Officer, Provident Hospital of Cook County, replied that there are
eighty-five to ninety vacancies in rad iology, nursing, and pharmacy. He further stated the transfer is
needed to also facilitate capital projects as well as the numerous repai rs that were dictated by the Joint
Commission on Accreditation of Healthcare Organizations (JCAHO) and the Illinois Department of
Public Health.
In response to Commissioner Peraica's inquiry regarding the pharmacy, Mr. Fairman replied the
pharmacy project is ahead of schedule, and will likely open early next year.
Chairman Daley noted that, on page 345, the number of vacancies is listed as twenty-eight.
Ms. Dunni ngs noted that page 345 lists only the vacancies that have been open longer than one year.
Vice Chairman Steele inquired as to where funds come from when vacant positions are fill ed.
Ms. Dunnings replied that funds are transferred from other vacant positions w ithin the same institution .
Commissioner Peraica asked Johnny C. Brown, Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook
County, why the hospital has a $500,000 deficit at mid-year.
Mr. Brown reiterated the problem that the issue of staffing presents, s pecifically in nursing, pharmacy,
laboratory, and radiology.
Commissioner Peraica voiced concern that $7,000,000 will not be enough fund s for Stroger Hospital of
Cook County, given its need for funds so far this year.
Mr. Brown replied that efficiencies are being implemented in non-patient areas.
Comm issioner Peraica inquired why additional funding is needed for the current parking management
service.
Mr. Brown replied that an increase is anticipated in association with the contract renegotiation.
Alvin Holley, C hief Financial Officer, Bureau of Health Services stated that in October of 2005, it was
not clear as to what the contract increase would be.

160

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Mr. Brown and Mr. Holley agreed to provide Commissioner Peraica with the total amount of the contract.
In response to Commi ssioner Peraica's questions as to the duration of the contract, Mr. Holley replied that
the parking management contract is for two years.
Commissioners Pera ica and Qui gley voiced concern about the extent to which parking is subsidi zed by
non-competiti ve rates.
Chairman Daley urged the commissioners to meet with Dr. Winship if they have any further
recommendations.
Wi th regard to Budgetary Unit 897, Account 449, "Operation, Maintenance and Repair of Institutional
Equipment," Commissioner Peraica inquired as to why the funds are needed, g iven that Stroger Hospital
of Cook County is new.
Mr. Brown stated that the Hospital is five years old, and that warranties have expired, and there are costs
associated w ith routine maintenance contracts.
In response to Commissioner Peraica 's inquiry as to whether the need for these funds is tied to any
litigation regarding the system that was installed, Mr. Brown replied not to his knowledge.

Commissioner Peraica requested that Jerry Robinson, Superintendent, Juvenile Temporary Detention
Center (JTDC), provide some details regarding the JTDC's transfer of funds request.
Mr. Robinson stated that the transfer of funds will be utilized mostly for overtime, which is necessary
given the thirty-five open positions. Most of these positions are for detention counselors. Other open
positions include caseworkers, medical department staff, nurses, psychologists and a physician. Recently,
approximately ten employees were hired. There are approximately 516 positions allocated in the budget,
and the vacancy rate is approximately I 0%.
Ms. Dunnings provided the following calculation: the cost for salary and benefits for 516 JTDC
employees, at an average salary of $40,000, and including $8,000 in benefits, would total approximately
$29,000,000.
Mr. Robinson further stated that the amount of money that will be required to comply with the
Supplemental Implementation Plan has not yet been determined. He believes that the amount of money
required to implement the Memorandum of Agreement has been included in the original budget. The
JTDC is applying for grants from the Annie E. Casey Foundation and the like, in order to be able to
upgrade their computer system, and for other projects.

Commissioner Sims, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved approval of the transfer of funds
request for the Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial Coordination. The motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen voted present, and Commissioners Gorman, Goslin, Quigley and Silvestri
voted no.

SECTION 9
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the recommendation
is as follows:
279598

AN ORDINANCE DEA LING WITH TEMPORARY ABSENCE IN THE OFFICE OF THE
PRESIDENT (PROPOSED ORDINANCE). Subm itting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
Larry Suffredin and Gregg Goslin, County Commissioners; Co-Sponsored by Elizabeth Ann
Doody Gorman, Joan Patricia Murphy and Peter N. Silvestri, County Commi ssioners.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE DEALING WITH TEMPORARY ABSENCE
IN THE OFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government pursuant to the 1970
Illinois Constitution, Article VII, Section 6(a); and

WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule power, the County of Cook may exercise any power
and perform any function rel ating to its government and affairs protecting health, safety and
welfare; and
WHEREAS, the 25th Amendment to the United States Constitution creates a process to
address a temporary, voluntary absence of the President of the United States; and
WHEREAS, Cook County, in order to properly manage its government and affairs, needs to
address a temporary, voluntary absence of the office of the President of the Cook County
Board; and
WHEREAS, to protect the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of Cook County and in
order to ensure that the government of Cook County has an Acting Executive with the duties
and powers of the President if the elected President declares that he/she is temporarily unable
to discharge the powers and duties of the office.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF
COMMISSIONERS, THAT:
Whenever the President transmits to the Board of Commissioners a written declaration that
he/she is unable to discharge the powers and duties of the office due to health or other
reasons; then the Board shall select and appoint one of their num ber to serve as Acting
President until the President transmits a written declaration to the Board of Commissioners
that he/she is able to discharge the powers and duties of the office of the President. T he
Acting President shall have all of the responsibilities, powers and duties of the office of the
President while servi ng as Acting President. The President shall continue to receive the pay
and benefits of the Office of the President during any such temporary absence.

NOTE: This item was also referred to the Committee on Rules.
279599).

(See Comm. No.

*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/20/06.
COMMISSIONER SUFFREDIN, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER QUIGLEY, MOVED TO
RECEIVE AND FILE COMMUNICATION NO. 279598. THE MOTION CARRIED.
