Your Committee has considered the following item:
279600

M INORITY AND WOMEN-OWNED BUSINESS ENTERPRISE COMPLIANCE
RESOLUTION (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored
by Earlean Collins, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

MINORITY AND WOMEN-OWNED BUSINESS ENTERPRISE
COMPLIANCE RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII
Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and
perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and

266

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, it is the policy of the County of Cook to create equal oppo rtunities in the award
of or participation in County contracts and to eliminate arbitrary barriers to full and equitable
opportunities for participation, as both prime and sub-contractors, in s uch contracts by
businesses certified as MBEs and WBEs; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Minority and WomenOwned Business Enterprise Ordinance (" MBE/WBE Ordinance") which establishes a goal of
award ing not Jess than thirty-five percent (35%) of the annual total dollar amount of County
contracts to certified MBEs and WBEs; and
WHEREAS, set backs from a 2000 Federal court case, 123 F. Supp. 2d 1087 (N. D. Ill.
2000), which invalidated some set aside programs for MBEs and WBEs, has resulted in a
conti nuous decrease in the number of MBE and WBE participation in County contracts; and
WHEREAS, while there has been some efforts made in bringing the County ' s Ordinance in
compliance with Federal Jaw and moving toward reaching the County's goal of creating equal
opportunity in the award of or participation in County contracts the urgency of the situation
and the difficulty of minority businesses to stay open due to the heavy reliance on County
contracts calls for the need of a public hearing to address the concerns of the County, MB Es
and WBEs.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that a publ ic hearing be conducted by the
Business and Economic Committee to determine the County's compliance with the
MBE/WBE Ordinance and federal law on MBE and WBE contract participation, to get
proper feed back from MBE and WBE participants, and to ascertain what can be done to
create greater opportunities for MBE and WBE participation in County contracts including
professional service contracts.
*Referred to the Business and Economic Development Committee on 06/20/06.
Chairman Collins called on Patrick T . Driscoll, Jr., Deputy State's Attorney, Chief, Civi l Actions Bureau,
State' s Attorney' s Office, to address the Committee.
Patrick Driscoll stated that in 1996 a lawsuit was filed against Cook County challenging the
Minority/Women Business Preference Ordinance, it was fi led by contractors and challenged only the
constitutionality of the Ordinance as it relates to construction projects. A trial was held in 2000 before
Judge Gready in the United States District Court. The court entered an order invalidating the Ordinance,
finding that it was unconstitutional as it applied to construction contracts . It has not been enforced since
the year 2000; at this time it only applies to non-construction contracts. The decision was appealed to the
United States Court of Appeals, and in July of 200 I the Federal Court of Appeals in Chicago affi rmed
Judge Gready' s decision, finding that his ana lysis was correct that there wasn' t suffic ient evidence shown
during the trial to justify the percentages that were set aside fo r women and minority business owners.
Further, there was a companion case brought agai nst the C ity of Chicago by the same plaintiffs that was
tried before Judge Moran several years ago; Judge Moran fo und that the City of Chicago's Ordinance as it
relates to construction projects had the same evidentiary deficiencies as the Cook County Ordinance.
Chairman Collins called on Betty Hancock Perry, Office of Contract Compliance, to address the
Comm ittee.

267

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Ms. Hancock Perry stated that in the past year the Office of Contract Compliance reviewed and revised
the certification process. The Office of Contract Compliance has revised the procedure for contract
review and monitoring. Further, her staff is responsible for certification, contract reviewing, and contract
monitoring and processing for all of Cook County. In the past year the Office of Contract Compliance
looked at how it could improve the process; one of the things was to take the certification process and
review it line-by-line and make sure that the information that was being requested from vendors is in fact
information that will help the Office of Contract Compliance make a determination as to whether or not
the company is owned and controlled by a woman or a minority individual. In the area of construction,
the Ordinance was struck down with regards to women and minority business enterprises being involved
in construction or being included. Over the past year the Office of Contract Compliance has looked at the
process and determined that while the participation may not be as high as it was in previous years there
still is substantial participation for women and minorities in construction. Ms. Hancock Perry stated that
the Office of Contract Compliance is implementing a new training program for purchasing individuals
who are within Cook County and using departments. A training session has been set up for individuals to
come in on a bi-weekly basis to work together with the Office of Contract Compliance. The Office of
Contract Compliance can only do what is intended in the Ordinance.
Chairman Collins called Janet K. Williams, Contract Administrator, Office of the Purchasing Agent, to
address the Committee.
Ms. Williams stated that the Office of the Purchasing Agent is the agency that procures goods and
services at the best market price for all of Cook County agencies. There are approximately 55 employees
in the Office of the Purchasing Agent and the website provides a listing of all the current bid proposals.
There are four types of contracts that the Office of the Purchasing Agent deal s with: I) the open market
or request for quotes are contracts that are under $25,000, are informal bids which are awarded to the
lowest bidder meeting specifications, are not awarded by the County Board, and the quotes are solicited
and received by mail, fax or telephone; 2) sole source contracts are contracts of any amount, but those
contracts are for commodities that must be available only through one manufacturer or they are
specialized items, Board authorization that is required, and it takes about four to six weeks to be
processed; 3) formal bids are requests for bids, are for items over $25,000, awarded to the lowest
responsive bidder meeting specifications, are a sealed bid process in which vendors are solicited through a
vendors list, Board authorization is required, and those contracts take approximately six to eight weeks to
be processed; and 4) Request for Proposals ( RFP) are handled directly by the individual using
departments. Ms. Williams listed some recommendations for the contractors: make sure that the entire
contract is completed; if the contract requires site inspection then be sure to attend; the contract must
comply with the MBE/WBE participation (the only contracts that do not require that are open market
contract under $25,000; read the special conditions and the specification pages before putting in the
amounts; comply w ith the specifications as they are written; complete the execution forms; and if the
contractor is a local Cook County business make sure the space is checked.
Chairman Collins asked Randolph M. Johnston, Assistant State' s Attorney, Deputy Supervisor,
Transactions and Health Law Unit, State' s Attorney's Office, to address the Committee regarding the
RFP process.
Mr. Johnston stated that the RFP process is an alternative process. The RFP process is meant if you're in
essence going to purchase the company's reputation, the company's prior performance because there is a
unique need for the particular type of service. Cook County has an RFP process which lets prospective
proposers know that a County agency is interested and a packet exists with information describing the
services being sought and instructions to the proposer on how the proposal is to be put together and
submitted to the County. The us ing department will often develop a committee to evaluate the proposals
that are received. Once the process is completed and the using department has identified one or more

268

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

vendors, the vendors are notified and then the County enters into a process of negotiating a contract with
those prospective vendors and then the contract would have to go through the nonnal contracting process.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

COOK COUNTY JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER ST ATUS
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII
Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constituti on, and as such may exercise any power and
perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, Cook County government has the responsibility for funding, operating and
monitoring the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety
and welfare of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordi nances on j uvenile
detention; and
WHEREAS, over the past several years there has been increasing allegations in reference to
the treatment of children, the quality of staff, management and operating procedures which
has resulted in litigati on; and
WHEREAS, the parties to litigation have been in talks to resolve the concerns over the
Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Federal Court approved an Agreed Supplemental Order between the
litigants; and
WHEREAS, it is essential that the Board review and ascertain the fiscal impact of
implementation of the May 2006 Ag reed Supplemental Order on the FY07 budget; and
WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Board review the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement,
the Juvenile Detention Alternative Initiative (JOA!) Self-Assessment Report, the
Implementation Plan, legal fees, and the progress made towards implementing the
requirements as set forth in the May 2006 Agreed Supplemental Order, the 2002
Memorandum of Agreement and the recommendations as set forth in the JDAI SelfAssessment Report, the Annie E. Casey Foundation Report and the John Howard Association
Report.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this Board conduct a public hearing in
which the above mentioned documents and issues are reviewed and addressed.
Note:

This item was also referred to the Finance Committee. (See Communication No.
279320.)

Commissio ner Peraica asked Patrick T. Driscoll, Jr., Deputy State's Attorney, Chief, C ivil Actions
Bureau, State's Attorney's Offi ce, to provide some c larification as to the nature and status of the
implementation plan.
Mr. Driscoll replied that Michael Mahony and C harles Fasano will conti nue in their duties; additionally,
four experts have been retained: Dr. Lo uis Kraus, Dr. David Roush, Carl Sanneti and Dr. Michael Cohen.
Brenda Welsh has been reta ined as the compliance administrator.
Commissio ner Peraica inquired as to who will be pay ing these individuals.
Mr. Driscoll replied that the County will be pay ing these individuals on an hourly basis so as to comply
with the Agreed Supplemental O rder. He emphasized that arrangements for these personne l are the res ult
of lengthy negotiations among plaintiffs' attorneys, the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center (JTDC)
personnel and County representatives. He further emphasized that these experts possess extensive
experience in the areas of correctio ns, psychiatric and medical operations and the like. He stated that all
of the individua ls involved are working toward an implementation plan that is practicable and in
compliance with the Memorandum of Agreement.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the fact that Mr. Mahoney wi ll not o nly be evaluating the
conditions but also monitoring them presents a conflict of interest.
Mr. Driscoll replied in the negative, stating that he believes that Mr. Mahoney is both an objecti ve and
able individual. He noted Mr. Mahoney's numerous years of experience in the area of corrections, his
work as former Director of the John Howard Associatio n, and the fact that he is one of the court moni tors
on the Duran case.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether these individuals would be evaluati ng the conditi ons and then
consulting with the appropriate residents, employees and Cook County officials.
Mr. Driscoll affirmed this, and stated that such activity is o ngoing.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether this investi gation would result in a written plan.
Mr. Driscoll replied in the affirmative. He stated that this plan would be shared with everyone and that
hopefully, with the input of all of the indi viduals involved, it wo uld be possible to implement this plan
withi n six months. He stated that he believes everything is on schedule.
Commissioner Peraica inquired which segments of the operati ons wi ll be studied.
Mr. Driscoll replied that all aspects of the Juvenil e Temporary Detention Center will be studied, including

COOK COUNTY JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER STATUS
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII Section 6(a)
of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and perform any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and

WHEREAS, Cook County government has the responsibi lity for fund ing, operating and mon itoring the
Cook County Juvenil e Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety and welfare
of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on juvenile detention; and
WHEREAS, over the past several years there has been increasing allegations in reference to the
treatment of chi ldren, the quality of staff, management and operating procedures which has resulted in
litigation; and

WHEREAS, the parties to litigation have been in talks to resolve the concerns over the Juveni le
Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Federal Court approved an Agreed Supplemental Order between the litigants; and

278

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, it is essential that the Board review and ascertain the fiscal impact of implementation of the
May 2006 Agreed Supplemental Order on the FY07 budget; and
WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Board review the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement, the Juvenile
Detention Alternati ve Initiative (JDAI) Self-Assessment Report, the Implementation Plan, legal fees, and
the progress made towards implementing the requirements as set forth in the May 2006 Agreed
Supplemental Order, the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement and the recommendations as set forth in the
JDAI Self-A ssessment Report, the Annie E. Casey Foundation Report and the John Howard Association
Report.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this Board conduct a public hearing in which the above
mentioned documents and issues are reviewed and addressed.

275835

AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING AND ENACTING THE CODE OF ORDINANCES OF
COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS AND PROVIDING FOR PENAL TIES FOR VIOLATION
THEREOF AND FOR THE AMENDMENT AND REPEAL OF CERTAIN COOK
COUNTY ORDINANCES (PROPOSED ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance
sponsored by John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners; CoSponsored by Jerry Butler, Forrest C laypool, Earlean Collins, John P. Daley, Elizabeth Ann
Doody Gorman, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Roberto Maldonado, Joan Patricia Murphy,
Anthony J. Peraica, Mike Quigley, Peter N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and
Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners.
I herewith submit to the Clerk of the Cook County Board of Commissioners, for approval by
the Board of Commissioners, a proposed ordinance enacting a Code of Ordinances of Cook
County, Illinois.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING AND ENACTING THE CODE OF ORDINANCES OF
COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS AND PROVIDING FOR PENALTIES FOR
VIOLATION THEREOF AND FOR THE AMENDMENT AND REPEAL OF
CERTAIN COOK COUNTY ORDINANCES
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois (" Board"), is the
legislative body of the County of Cook ("County"), a home rule unit of local government as
provided for in the Illinois Constitution of I 970, and in this capacity the Board adopts
Ordinances and Resolutions which apply within and pertain to the affairs of the County; and
WHEREAS, the Ordinances and Resolutions adopted by the Board are numbered and made
avai Iable to the public by the Clerk of Cook County, Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Board desires to adopt a codified version of its Ordi nances and Resolutions
which shall be known as the "Code of Ordinances of Cook County, Illinois" or the "Cook
County Code," utilizing subject matter divisions and a convenient numbering system
reviewed by the State's Attorney of Cook County and approved by the Board; and
WHEREAS, this Board desires that the Cook County Code be published and updated
regu larly, and has contracted with the Municipal Code Corporation to perform these fu nctions
and to make the Cook County Code avail able to the public on the internet through a link
placed on the County's website located at www.cookcountygov.com and the Cook County
Clerk's website located at www.cookctyclerk.com; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Code, as adopted by this Ordinance, includes provisions for
the amendment and repeal of Ordinances and Resolutions previously adopted by the Board
and for the continued validity of certain Ordinances and Resolutions previously adopted by
the Board, and also includes provision for the imposition of penalties for violations of the
Cook County Code.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:

Commissioner Suffredin requested that James L. Eldridge, Jr., Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of
Administration, and ASA Helen Haynes, Supervisor, Transactions and Health Law Unit, State ' s
Attorney ' s Office, make some remarks regarding the process that has lead up to this Ordinance.
Mr. Eldridge stated that this project was made a priority by President Stroger. Thi s compiled and codified
code will not only be invaluable to the legal profession, but also to all the citizens of Cook County. As
directed through an amendment in the 1996 budget, industrial engineers prepared a leg islative reference
bureau study in which the primary recommendation was to codify the County's ordinances prior to
establishing a legislative reference bureau. Codifying the County Code was the task which this gro up was
directed to accom plish. I have to emphasize the amount of effort that went into codifying the County' s
code. This group has been working together for over two years on this project and has put in hundreds of
hours. This project would not have moved fo rward without the tremendous effort and resources of the
State's Attorney' s Office. They were instrumental in reviewing every single word in the Code. Also
playing major roles in this project were the following people: Jack Weinrauch, Assistant to the President;
Jerry Pray, Industrial Eng ineer; Elizabeth Reidy, Deputy Bureau Chief, Civil Actions Bureau, State's
Attorney' s Office; Sara Hynes, Assistant State ' s Attorney, State' s Attorney's; Office; Joy Wykowski,

Counsel, Office of Commissioner Larry Suffredin; Michelle Devine, former Director of

special recognition to Catherine Maras O' Leary, Chief Information Officer, Bureau of Information
Technology and Automation; Karen Griffin, Assistant to the Chief Information Officer; La ura Lechowicz
Felicione, Special Assistant to the Pres ident; Michelle Harris, Secretary to the Board; Tom O' Brien,
Assistant to Commissioner Hansen; Debbie Santana, Assistant to Commissioner Carl Hansen; and Roger
Meiriam, Municipal Code Corporation, who was responsible for preparing the County Code document.

AMENDMENT #2
MOTION TO AMEND AND TO RECOMMEND FOR APPROVAL, AS AMENDED,
THE COOK COUNTY CODE ADOPTION ORDINANCE OF 2006
It is hereby moved that the proposed Cook County Code Adoption Ordinance of 2006,
being considered by the Legislative and Intergovernmental Affairs Committee of the
Cook County Board of Comm issioners on June 27, 2006, be amended as set forth on the
s ubmitted proposed Ordinance and that such proposed Ordinance, as amended, be
recommended for approval by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

Chairman Suffredin offered the following clarification: In Section 3, page 3 of the Ordinance, for the
purposes of this code adoption Ordinance of 2006, any legislation adopted by the Board prior to October
I, 2006, that contains provisions that are of a general and permanent nature, shall be considered an
Ordinance. Instructions exist in the code directing Commissioners only to present Ordinances, not
resolutions.
Commissioner Peraica, seconded by Chairman Suffredin, moved the approval of the Amendment
#2 to the Ordinance.
Commissioner Coll ins inquired whether the "whereas" clauses/purpose/declaration of intent are going to
be eliminated as a result of this Ordinance.
Commissioner Suffredin replied that this code includes only an "action" section not, " whereas c lauses."
Another ordinance, drafted by Jack Weinrauch on a Legislative Reference Bureau, is pending. This
ordinance would create an Office of Legislative Counsel for the Board. Chapter One of the revised Code
contains instructions regarding how to draft an ordinance, as distinguished from a memorializing
resolution . I hope in the next budget session we will have legislative counsel to advise us regarding form
and substance. In the meantime, I have as ked the State's Attorney's Office to work with the
Commiss ioners upon the adoption of this Ordinance, to help them understand the format. As a result, we
should have consistency and it should be easier to amend this Code. This Code will be printed in the
volumes distributed to all Commissioners in February. It w ill also be available online and in cd format.
This presents a tremendous opportunity for the citizens to know the law. This format is the exact same
format used in the current State of lllinois statutes.
Vice Chairman Silvestri s uggested that the distinction between a resolution and an ordinance could be
made under the Rules of the Board.
Chairman Suffredin reiterated the sizable contribution that Jack Weinrauch made to this effort. He
requested that Assistant State' s Attorney Haynes provide a short overview of the how we got to this point.
Assistant State's Attorney Haynes stated that the first motion corrects severa l errors in the draft. The
second motion contains general language allowing the C lerk, in collaboration with the State's Attorney's
Office and Mr. Weinrauch ' s Office, to instruct Munic ipal Code Corporation to make certain technical
changes . When the document is published it will be reader-friendly. This may require some reordering.
The process started several years ago. We requested that a document with underlining and strikeout be
generated to show the changes that were made to the original ordinances. In several areas, the ordinances
are particularly out-of-date. Several ordinances from the Bureau of Health Services and Building Code
fall into that category. We' ve retained these provisions without including them in the Code, in case you
wish to update them through the supplement process; Municipal Code Corporation is under contract to
supplement this periodically.

287

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006
Chairman Suffredin noted that the State of Illinois has a revisory statute that deals with the clean up of
ordinances.
Commissioner Peraica stated that an indexing component and a central staff that could work with the
Commissioners in terms of historical and legislative research would be excellent additions to this system.
Chairman Suffredin noted that he maintains a legislative library containing all the enactments since he has
been in office. He is eagerly looking to turn this over to someone who might perform this role or
someone in Board Secretary Michelle Harris' office. History of who introduced ordinances, how this was
amended, when they were passed, in order to give lawyers, judges, etc., the tools they need.
Vice Chairman Si lvestri noted that the effective date of the Ordinance is October 1, 2006.
Commissioner Peraica, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved the approval of Amendment
#2 to the Ordinance. T he motion carried.
Chairman Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved the approval of Communication
No. 275835, as amended. The motion carried.

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.,

THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,

PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING AND ENACTING
THE CODE OF ORDINANCES OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS
AND PROVIDING FOR PENALTIES FOR VIOLATION THEREOF AND FOR THE
AMENDMENT AND REPEAL O F CERTAIN COOK COUNTY ORDINANCES
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois ("Board"), is the legislative body of
the County of Cook ("County"), a home rule unit of local government as provided for in the Illinois
Constitution of 1970, and in this capacity the Board adopts Ordinances and Resolutions which apply
within and pertain to the affairs of the County; and
WHEREAS, the Ordinances and Resolutions adopted by the Board are numbered and made available to
the public by the Clerk of Cook County, Illinois; and

288

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the Board desires to adopt a codified version of its Ordinances and Resolutions which shall
be known as the "Code of Ordinances of Cook County, Illinois" or the "Cook County Code," utilizing
subject matter divisions and a convenient numbering system reviewed by the State's Attorney of Cook
County and approved by the Board; and

WHEREAS, this Board desires that the Cook County Code be published and updated regularly, and has
contracted with the Municipal Code Corporation to perform these function s and to make the Cook County
Code available to the public on the internet through a link placed on the County's website located at
www.cookcountygov.com and the Cook County Clerk's website located at www.cookctyclerk.com; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Code, as adopted by this Ordinance, includes provisions for the
amendment and repeal of Ordinances and Resolutions previously adopted by the Board and for the
continued validity of certain Ordinances and Resolutions previously adopted by the Board, and a lso
includes provision for the imposition of penalties for violations of the Cook County Code.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK
COUNTY, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. Designation of Adopting Ordinance. This Ordinance, which provides for the adoption of a
Code of Ordinances of Cook County, Illinois, shall be known as the "Cook County Code Adoption
Ordinance of2006."

Section 2. Adoption of Code. The document entitled the "Cook County Code, a Code of Ordinances of
Cook County, Illinois," a copy of which is submitted herewith, is hereby adopted. The Cook County
Code shall be binding and effective as to the ordinances included therein.

Section 3. Legislation of a General and Permanent Nature. For purposes of this Cook County Code
Adoption Ordinance of 2006, any legislation adopted by the Board that contains provisions that are of a
general and permanent nature shall be considered an "ordinance" irrespective of any designation of such
legislation as a "resolution" of the Board.

Section 4. Ordinances Omitted from Code Saved. Notwithstanding any other the provision of this
Cook County Code Adoption Ordinance of 2006, any ordinance inadvertently or intentionally omitted
fro m the Cook County Code shall be binding and effective as adopted by the County Board and shall be
maintained on file with the Cook County Clerk.

Section 5. Additions or Amendments to Cook County Code; Supplements. Ordinances which add to
or amend the Cook County Code and which are adopted by the Board after November 1, 2005 shall be
incorporated into the Cook County Code and the Cook County Code shall be deemed to include such
Ordinances as of the date of their adoption. Such Ordinances shall be published in supplements issued at
the direction of the Cook County C lerk at least annually and in the manner set forth in the Cook County
Code. Such Supplements may be incorporated into the primary document known as the Cook County
Code as directed by the Cook County C lerk and without further action by the Board, as provided in the
Cook County Code.

Section 6. Penalties for Code Violations. Unless another penalty is expressly provided in the Cook
County Code, a violation of any provision of the Code or any rule or regulation adopted in accordance
therewith shall, upon conviction, be punishable by a fine not exceeding $1 ,000.00, as provided in Section
1-10 of the Cook County Code, as adopted.

289

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Section 7. Exercise of Home Rule Authority. This Cook County Code Adoption Ordinance of 2006
and the Cook County Code adopted hereby is an exercise of the home rule powers granted to the County
of Cook under Article VII, Section 6 of the Illinois Constitution of 1970.

Section 8. Effective Date. This Cook County Code Adoption Ordinance of 2006 shall be effective upon
passage.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

ENTERPRIZ COOK COUNTY BOARD (APPOINTMENT)
Transmitting a
Communication from John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners:
I hereby appoint Mr. AGOSTINO LORENZINI to the Enterpriz Cook County Board, for a
term to begin immediately.
I s ubmit this communication for your approval.

*Referred to the Committee on Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations on March
15, 2006.
Mr. Agostino Lorenzini stated that he understands the significance of having an organization such as
Enterpriz Cook County Board in order to assist in the development of economic areas of the County that
are really in need. He hopes to bring his experience and acumen to aid him in this process.
Commissioner Daley strongly recommended Mr. Lorenzini. He stated that Mr. Lorenzi worked for the
County and for him for a number of years; he was an outstanding legi slative aide and administrative
assistant. He would help this Board tremendously.
C hairman Suffredin stated that there is no question that Mr. Lorenzi is the choice of President Stroger; the
letter from the President predates the president' s illness, and Mr. Lorenzini has indicated that he has had
conversations with the President.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether this position is pro bono.
Mr. Lorenzi ni replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Peraica commended Mr. Lorenzini on his academic and professional experience. He
inquired as to what two issues Mr. Lorenzini would want to focus on in terms of the Cook County
Southland's high unemployment rate and the economic desolation that exists in certain of its sections.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

several efforts underway in terms of tax reactivation programs. These items were, a year ago, high on Mr.
Pechous' agenda, and included an effort to bring in federal tax dollars to encourage business to locate or
relocate within economically challenged economic areas. Also, the Enterpriz Cook County Board has an
ongoing effort to bring in new members.
Vice Chairman Silvestri congratulated Mr. Lorenzini ' s work in the public sector, stating that he is
confident that Mr. Lorenzini will be an asset to the Board.

REAL ESTATE MANAGEMENT DIVISION, by John W. Davis, Director, transmitting a
Communication, dated May 3 I, 2006:
requesting authorization to enter into and execute a three-year extension agreement with 69
West Washington Management Company, LLC. ("69 WWMC"), for the continued
management and operation of the 69 West Washington Building (the " Building") pursuant to
the Management Agreement approved by th is Board on August 7, 1997 (the "Contract"),
previously extended by a first amendment to Management Agreement approved by this Board
on June 20, 2000, and by a second amendment to Management Agreement approved by this
Board on July I, 2003. The contract expires July 31 , 2006.
Submitted with this letter is a copy of the proposal for extension, including a summary of the
accomplishments of 69 West Washington Management Company during the current term.
The proposed extension will be on a ll the terms and conditions contained in the contract, as
previously amended, including the annual increase based on the Consumer Price Index.
C urrently, the management fee is $ 177,525 per year.
Oversight and supervision of 69 WWMC is by the Real Estate Management Division, with
dual responsibility by the Director of Facilities Management, John T. Joiner, as to physical
conditions, renovation and services to the building.
Mr. Joiner concurs in th is
recommendation.
Approval recommended.

*Referred To The Real Estate Subcommittee 04/05/06.
Comm issioner Peraica asked Mr. Davis who are the principals of the management company of the LLC.
John W. Davis, Director, Real Estate Management Division, replied that the principals are U.S. Equities
and East Lake Corporation; those principals of that corporation form the LLC.
Comm issioner Peraica voiced his concern on the original agreement that provides the exclusive rights for
69 WWMC to manage 69 West Washington.
Anna Ashcraft, Special Assistant to the President stated it is a management agreement in which the owner
would enter into with a managing company where they enter into contracts on the County ' s behalf for
janitorial and security services. The company assists in negotiating leases, and makes recommendations
on improvements and maintenance of the building. The company also submits a budget every year which
is reviewed and approved by the Real Estate Management Division. A typical management agreement is
a three year term and the Real Estate Management Division returns to the Board of Commissioners when
the term is abo ut to expire. The original agreement began on August I, 1997.

279592

REAL ESTATE MANAGEMENT DIVISION, by John W. Davis, Director, Michael F.
Sheahan, Sheriff of Cook County by Robert E. Beavers, Chief Deputy Sheriff, Court Services
Division, transmitting a Communication, dated May 31, 2006:
requesting approval of the First Amendment to Contract No. 01-54-528 Rebid with

JONETTE PRODUCTS ENTERPRISE, LTD., Chicago, Illinois, to provide food service
management at the Criminal Court Administration Building including operation of the
cafeteria for food service to the public and for preparation of meals for delivery to jurors and
judges.
Prior to expiration of the contract in 2004, the Office of Capital Planning and Policy had
proposed a renovation of the kitchen and cafeteria area, and the Board of Commissioners
approved an extension to the contract on July 13, 2004, expiring June 12, 2006, since rebidding the contract was not practical while renovation plans and construction were under
way.
Plans are now complete and the Office of Capital Planning and Policy is ready to begin
construction, which should be completed within nine to twelve months. The cafeteria and
kitchen areas will not be usable during construction, and food service to the general public
will not be available. However, the current contractor, Janette Products Enterprises, Ltd., is
willing and able to provide meals for judges and jurors service from $3.89 per judge' s meal
and $3.83 per jury meal , which represents the base amount established in the contract, with a
cost of living increase annually. In addition, the number of meals required has increased
from approximately 66,365 in 200 I to 105,000 today, due to the increased number of trials
occurring as the judiciary attempts to reduce the backlog of cases.
Under the terms of the First Amendment, the contract with the current vendor would be
extended for a period of one year, and increased to provide for the increased number of meal s
and the CPI increase. Rent paid under the contract by the vendor will be waived once
construction commences, since the space will be unavailable for use. The county has the
option to tenninate at any time with a thirty day notice, so that once construction is complete
and another contract has been awarded, this contract will be terminated.

272037

AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING THE BOUNDARIES OF EACH OF TH E 17
COUNTY COMMISSIONER DISTRICTS BY STREET LOCATION (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Sponsored by Larry Suffredin, County Commissioner. Transmitting a
Communication, dated June 28, 2005.
The County board is required by law to redistrict after each decenn ial census to insure that
the 17 County Commissioner Districts are of equal population according to the census data
from the U.S. Census Bureau. The last redistricting plan was approved in 200 I.
This ordinance replaces the boundaries of each district, as defined by technical tracts of land
in 200 I, with boundaries defined by street locations. This ordinance does not affect the
boundaries of any district. Instead, the changes will aid with the codification of Cook
County 's laws.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
The metes and bounds descriptions of this ordinance have been designed to describe exactly
the same areas that were described in the census tract and block description used when these
districts were created in 200 I. Absent an undetected error, there is no difference in the "new"
descriptions of the districts from those used in the 2002 elections and in the Primary Election
earlier this year.
The Clerk of Cook County is given authority to make any clerical or technical changes to
conform the 200 I ordinance to this ordinance.

ORDINANCES
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I transmit herewith a proposed O rd inance to be considered by this Honorable Body.
T his O rdin ance has been recommended by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois, pursuant to
the Wages of Employees on Public Wo rks (Prevailing Wage Act, Illino is Revised Statutes, codified as
amended, 820 I LCS 130/1 et seq. ( 1993), form erly 111. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s- I et seq.).

06-0-30
ORDINANCE
WHERE AS, the State of Illinois has enacted "An Act regul ating wages of laborers, mechanics and other
workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body or any political
subdi vision or by any one under contract for public works," approved June 26, I 94 1, codified as
amended, 820 I LCS 130/1 et seq. ( I 993), formerly Ill. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s- l et seq.; and

34 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 2, 2006

WHEREAS, the aforesaid Act requires that the Board of Commissioners of the County of Cook
investigate and ascertain the prevailing rate of wages as defined in said Act for laborers, mechanics and
other workers in the locality of said County employed in performing construction of public works, for
said County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE
COMMISSIONERS OF THE COUNTY OF COOK:

PRESIDENT

AND

BOARD OF

Section 1. To the extent and as required by "An Act regulating wages of laborers, mechanics and other
workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body or any pol itical
subdivision or by any one under contract for public works," approved June 26, I 94 I, as amended, the
general prevailing rate of wages in this locality for laborers, mechanics and other workers engaged in the
construction of public works coming under the jurisdiction of this County is hereby ascertained to be the
same as the prevailing rate of wages for construction work in the Cook County area as determined by the
Department of Labor of the State of Illinois as of June ~ 2006, a copy of that determination being
submitted he reto and incorporated herein by reference. As required by said Act, any and all revisions of
the prevailing rate of wages by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois shall supersede the
Department's June determination and apply to any and all public works construction undertaken by the
County of Cook. The Definiti on of any tenns appearing in this Ordinance which are also used in
aforesaid Act shall be the same as in said Act.
Section 2. Nothing herein contained shall be construed to apply said general prevailing rate of wages as
herein ascertained to any work or employment except public works construction of this County to the
extent required by the aforesaid Act.
Section 3. The Bureau of Human Resources shall publicly post or keep available for inspection by any
interested party in the main office of this Bureau of Human Resources (County) this determination or any
revisions of such prevailing rate of wage. A copy of this determination or of the current revised
determination of prevailing rate of wages then in effect shall be attached to all contract specifications.
Section 4. The C lerk shall mail a copy of this determination to any employer, and to any association of
employers and to any person or association of employees who have filed their names and addresses,
requesting copies of any determination stating the particular rates and the particular class of workers
whose wages will be affected by such rates.
Section 5. The Bureau of Human Resources sha ll promptly file a certified copy of this Ordinance with
both the Secretary of State Index Division and the Department of Labor of the State of Ill inois.
Section 6. The Bureau of Human Resources shall cause to be published in a newspaper of general
circulation within the area a copy of this Ordinance, and such publication shall constitute notice that the
determination is effective and that this is the determination of this public body.
Section 7. The Purchasing Agent of Cook County shall specify in the call for bids in any contract for
public works that the general prevailing rate of wages in the locality for each craft or type of laborer or
mechanic needed to execute the contract to perfonn such work, also the general prevailing rate for legal
holiday and overtime work as ascertai ned by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid for each craft
or type of work needed to execute the contract or to perform such work. The Purchasing Agent in
awarding the contract shall cause to be inserted in the contract a stipulation to the effect that not less than
the prevailing rate of wages, as found by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid to all laborers,
workers and mechanics performing work under the contract, and the Purchasing Agent shall also require
in all such contractor's bonds that the contract inc lude such provision as will guarantee the faithful
performance of such prevailing wage clause as provided by the contract.

342

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Section 8. In the case of any underpayment of the prevailing wage, a penalty of 20% of the
underpayment shall be assessed against the contractor or subcontractor; and the 20% penalty shall be
payable to the Illinoi s Department of Labor. Any underpayment that has not been repaid to a worker
within thirty-days of violation is subject to an additional 2% of the underpayment as a punitive damage
assessment. This is payable to the worker.
Section 9. There is an automatic two (2) year debarment of any contractor or subcontractor found to
have violated the Act on two (2) separate occasions. An affected contractor or subcontractor may request
the Department to hold a hearing on the alleged violations within ten ( 10) days notification of the second
violation.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 7, 2006 from
THOM AS J. GLASER, Chief Financial Officer
transmitting fo r your approva l an Ordi nance in support of the executio n of a line of credit for working
capital purposes to support the timely payments of general County expenses. Due to the timing of
scheduled payments of the Intergovernmental Transfer Agreement in both FY2006 and FY2007, as well
as delays in processing Medicaid payments by the State of Illinois, this line of credit may be drawn upon
to manage the County's overall cash flow needs.

344

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

06-0-31
ORDINANCE
An Ordinance authorizing the execution of an agreement for a line of credit and related
documents and the issuance of one or more prom issory notes in connection therewith.

WHEREAS, Section 6(a) of Article VI I of the 1970 Constitution of the State of lllinois provides
that "a County which has a Chief Executi ve Officer elected by the electors of the County ... (is) a Home
Rule Unit" and The County of Cook, lllinois (the "County"), has a Chief Executive Officer elected by the
electors of the County and is therefore a Home Rul e Unit and may, under the power granted by said
Section 6(a) of Article VI I of the Constitution of 1970. as supplemented by the Local Government Debt
Reform Act, as amended, the (" Act"), exercise any power and perform any function pertaining to its
government and affai rs, including, but not limited to, the power to tax and to incur debt; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to the provisions of the Act, the County has the power to incur debt
payable from any lawful source and maturing within 40 years from the time it is incurred without prior
refere ndum approval; and
WH EREAS, the Board of Commissioners of the County (the " Board") has not adopted any
ordinance, resolution, order or motion or provided any County Code provi sions which restrict or limit the
exercise of the home rule powers of the County in the issuance of general obligation full faith and credit
notes without referendum for corporate purposes or which provides any special rules or procedures for the
exercise of such power; and
WHEREAS, the Board hereby expressly determines that it is advisable, necessary and in the best
interests of the County that the County authorize the execution and delivery of an agreement for a line of
credit (the "Agreement"); and
WHEREAS, it is in the best interests of the inhabitants of the County and necessary for the
government and affairs of the County a lso to a uthorize the issuance of one or more promissory notes
(collecti vely , the "Note") to evidence the obligation to repay the principal of and interest on amounts
drawndown by the County under s uch Agreement; and
WHEREAS, to such end it is hereby deemed advisable and necessary that the Board now adopts
this ordinance so to specify, determine and authorize:
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of The County of
Cook, Illino is, as follows:

ARTICLE I.

DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATIO NS

Section I.I.
Definitions: The fo llowing words and terms used in this Ordinance shall have
the following meanings unless the context or use indicates another or different meaning:

"Agreement " means that certain written agreement providing for the creation of a line of credit
for the County and the issuance of one or more Notes to evidence the obligation of the County to repay
amounts due and owing thereunder.

345

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

"Act" means Section 6(a) of Article VII of the 1970 Consti tution of the State of Illinois, as
supplemented and amended by the Local Government Debt Reform Act of the State of Illinois, as
amended, and the other Omnibus Bond Acts, as amended.
"Advance for Value" means a receipt of funds by the County under the Agreement and relative to
the Note which is a loan advance on and partial purchase price consideration for the Note, to be
evidenced as provided in the Note form.
" Agreement" means the agreement to be executed by the County and providing for the advance
offunds to the County to defray the necessary expenses of the County for its corporate purposes.
" Board" means the Board of Commissioners of the County.
"Chief Financial Officer" means the Chief Financ ial Officer of the County.
"Code" means the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended.
"County" means The County of Cook, Illinois.

"Designated Officer " means the President, Chief Financial Officer or any other office or
employee of the County so designated by a written instrument signed by the President or the Chief
Financial Officer.
"Face Amount" means the authorized maximum amount of the Note, as stated on its face.
"Fixed Rate Note" means a Note bearing interest at a fixed rate percent per annum.
"Floating Rate Note" means a Note bearing interest at a rate percent per annum which is subject
to change from time to time, payable from time to time, and subject to various options for payment by the
owners thereof, as more fully provided for in the Agreement.
"Maturity Date" means the date on which the principal of the Note is due and owing under the
Agreement.

"Note Order" means the 2006 Note Order and Notification of Sale to be executed by the Chief
Financial Officer and setting forth certain details of the Agreement and the Note as hereinafter provided.
"Note Register " means the books of the County kept by the Note Registrar to evidence the
registration and transfer of the Note.
"Note Registrar " means the institution or person so designated and defined in the Note Order, or
successors or assigns.

"Ordinance" means this ordinance as originally introduced and adopted and as the same may
from time to time be amended or supplemented in accordance with the terms hereof.
"Paying Agent" means the institution, having fiduci ary power, or person so designated and
defined in the Note Order, or successors or assigns.
"Purchase Price " means the price paid to the County by the Purchaser fo r the Note.

346

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

"Purchaser" means the purchaser of the Note as so identified in the Note Order.
"Regular Record Date" means the fifteenth day before any interest payment date on the Note or
such other date as may be provided in the Note Order.
"Taxable " means, with reference to the Note, the status of interest paid and received thereon as
includable in the gross income of the owners thereof under the Code for federal income tax purposes.
"Tax Exempt" means, with respect to the Note, the status of interest paid and received thereon as
excludable from the gross income of the owners thereof under the Code for federal income tax purposes,
except to the extent that s uch interest is taken into account in computing an adjustment used in
determining the alternative minimum tax for certain corporations.

Section 1.2.
Severability oflnvalid Provisions: If any secti on, paragraph, c lause or provision of this
Ordinance shall be held invalid, the inval idity of such section, paragraph, clause or provision shall not
affect any of the other provi sions of this Ordinance.
Section 1.3.
Short Title: This Ordinance may hereafter be cited by the County or hereinafter referred
to as the Â·'2006 Line of Credit Ordinance."
ARTICLE II. DETERMINATIONS OF THE COUNTY
Section 2.1.

Findings: The Board hereby find s and determines that (A) all of the recitals contained in
the preambles to this Ordinance are full , true and correct and hereby incorporates them into this
Ordinance by this reference; (B) this Ordinance is adopted pursuant to Section 6 of Article VII of the
Illinois Constitution of 1970; (C) it is necessary and in the best interests of the County that the County
adopt this Ordinance; (D) it is necessary and in the best interests of the County that the Agreement be
executed so as to provide for the timely defray ing of necessary expenses inc urred by the County fo r its
corporate purposes; and (E) the execution of the Agreement, the borrowing of money for the purposes
authorized therein and the issuance of the Note is for a proper public purpose and is in the public interest.

Section 2.2.

Execution of the Agreement Authorized: The County is hereby authorized to enter
into the Agreement with the Purchaser in such fo rm as shall be approved by the C hief Financial Officer,
and by majority poll. not subject to ratification or cancellation by the Board or its members. of all
members of the Board. which form shall be as is deemed usual and customary in the municipal bond
market and may inc lude, without limitation, terms providing for posted security for one or more Notes,
assignment of taxes, drawdown conditions, repay ment provisions, and provisions for default, provided,
however, that in the event of any conflict between the terms and provisions of this Ordinance and the
Agreement, the terms and provisions of thi s Ordinance s hall in all events control. The Chief Financial
Officer be, and hereby is, authorized, empowered and directed to execute, and his executi on thereof shall
constitute conclusive evidence of the approval of any and al l terms contai ned in the Agreement by the
Board, and the County Clerk be, and hereby is, authorized, empowered and directed to attest the
Agreement in the name, for and on behalf of the County, and thereupon to cause the Agreement to be
delivered to the counterparty thereto. The Agreement (as executed) is entered into to provide fo r the loan
of the proceeds of the Note to the County and the use of such proceeds as aforesaid and to pay the costs of
issuing the Note, in the manner and with the effect therein provided. From and after the execution and
delivery of the Agreement, the officers, employees and agents of the County are hereby authorized,
empowered and directed to do all such acts and things and to execute all such documents as may be
necessary to carry out and comply with the provisions of the Agreement as executed; and the Agreement
shall constitute, and hereby is made, a part of this Ordinance, and a copy of the Agreement s hall be placed
in the official records of the County, and shall be available for public inspection at the office of the
County Clerk.

347

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J ULY 12, 2006

Section 2.3.
Note Authorized: For the purposes aforesaid, the Note is hereby authorized to be issued
as a drawdown note in the aggregate principal amount of not to exceed $200,000,000.
Section 2.4.
Note Details: The Note shall be issued in the principal amount of not to exceed
$200,000,000 and shall bear such title and series designation as the Chief Fi nancial Officer shall
determine in the Note Order. The Note may be a Fixed Rate Note or a Floating Rate Note as provided in
the Note Order. The Note shall be dated as of the first Advance for Value on the Note or as otherwise
provided in the Agreement (any such date being the " Dated Date"), and the amount of the Note issued,
being the sum of the amounts as shown as Advances for Value on the Note, not in excess of the Face
Amount, less in each case principal payments made from time to time thereon, shall be the "Outstanding
Principal Amount" of the Note. The Outstanding Principal Amount of the Note from time to time
outstanding shall bear interest at not to exceed a rate percent per annum which is ten percent (I 0.00%),
with interest payable on such date or dates as provided in the Agreement, upon any prepayment and on
the Maturity Date. The Maturity Date shall be not later than January 31 , 2008.
The Note shall bear interest on the Outstanding Principal Amount from time to time at the rate provided,
in each case from the time advanced until duly paid or provided for, such interest being computed upon
the basis of a 360-day year of twelve 30-day months.
Subject to the provisions of the Agreement, the interest on and all payments of principal of the Note shall
be payable in lawful money of the United States of America, or by electronic funds transfer of lawful
money of the United States of America, upon presentation at the office of the Note Registrar, provided,
however, that so long as a financial institution is the registered owner of the Note, then such payments
shall be made by check or draft of the Note Registra r to the person in whose name the Note is registered
as evidenced by the Note Register at the close of business on the applicable Regular Record Date, which
check or draft shall be payable in lawful money of the United States of America and mailed to the address
or transferred to such account of such registered owner as it appears on the Note Register or at such other
address or accou nt as may be furnis hed in writing to the Note Registrar, and provided, further, that the
final installment of principal of and interest on the Note shall be paid upon surrender in lawful money of
the United States of America, at the principal office maintained for the purpose by the Paying Agent or its
proper agent.
If so provided in the Note Order, the Note may be redeemable or prepayable prior to maturity at the
option of the County, in whole or in part on any date, upon such terms and at such times and at a
redemption or prepayment price of par plus accrued interest to the date of redemption or prepayment, as
determined by the Chief Financial Officer at the time of the sale thereof.
The Note shall have be substantially in the form attached to the Agreement and as approved by the Chief
Financial Officer, his execution thereof to constitute approval of all terms set forth therein by the Board,
and shall have impressed or imprinted thereon the corporate seal or facsim ile thereof of the County and
shall be signed by the manual or duly authorized facsimile signatures of the Chief Financial Officer and
County Clerk, as they shall determine, and in case any officer whose signature shall appear on the Note
shall cease to be such officer before the delivery of the Note, such signature shall nevertheless be valid
and sufficient for all purposes, the same as if such officer had remained in office until delivery.
The execution by the County of the fully registered Note shall constitute full and due authorization of the
Note, and the Note Registrar shall thereby be authorized to authenticate, date and deliver the Note. The
person in whose name the Note shall be registered shall be deemed and regarded as the absolute owner
thereof for a ll purposes, and payment of the principal of or interest on the Note shall be made only to or
upon the order of the registered owner thereof or the owner's legal representative. All such payments
shall be valid and effectual to satisfy and discharge the liability upon the Note to the extent of the sum or
sums so paid.

348

 JOURNA L OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

The Note shall have thereon a certificate of authentication du ly executed by the Note Registrar as
authenticating agent of the County and showing the date of authentication. The Note shall not be valid or
obligatory for any purpose or be entitled to any securi ty or benefit under this Ordinance unless and until
such certificate of authentication shall have been duly executed by the Note Reg istrar by manual
signature, and such certificate of authentic~tion upon the Note shall be conclusive evidence that the Note
has been authenticated and deli vered under th is Ordinance. The certificate of authentication on the Note
shall be deemed to have been executed by the Note Registrar if signed by an authori zed officer of the
Note Registrar.

Section 2.5.

Sale and Delivery of Note: The Chief Financial Officer is hereby authorized to sell all
or any portion of the Note to the Purchaser from time to time as the Chief Financial Officer shall
determine that the proceeds of such sales are needed and on such terms as he may deem to be in the best
interests of the County. Nothing contained in this Ordinance shall limit the sale of the Note or any
portion thereof or any maturity or maturities thereof at a price or prices in excess of the principal amount
thereof. Subsequent to the sale of the Note or subsequent to the sale of any portion thereof, the Chief
Financial Officer shall file in the office of the County C lerk a Note Order directed to the Board
identi fying (i) the terms of the sale, (i i) the amount, if any, of the Note be ing sold as a Floating Rate Note,
(iii) the Dated Date, (iv) the aggregate principal amount of the Note sold, (v) the repayment schedule for
the principa l of and interest on the Note, (vi) the optional redemption provisions, if any, applicable to the
Note, (vi i) whether the Note is Tax Exempt or Taxable and (viii) any other matte r authorized by this
Ordinance to be determined by the Chief Financial Officer at the time of sale of the Note, and thereafter
the Note as so sold shall be duly prepared and executed in the form and manner provided herein and
delivered to the Purchaser in accordance with the terms of sale.
Any Designated Officer and s uch other officers of the County as may be necessary are hereby authori zed
to execute such other documents, as may be necessary to implement the Agreement and the transactions
contemplated thereby and to effect the iss uance and de livery of the Note, and execution thereof by s uch
officers is hereby deemed conclusive evidence of approval thereof with such changes, additions,
insertions, omissions or deletions as such officers may determine, with no furt her official action of or
direction by the Board.

Section 2.6.
General Tax Covenants: The proceeds of the Note shall be used to provide funds fo r
the payment of necessary expenses incurred for the general corporate purposes of the County and to that
end shall be set aside in the Working Cash Fund (the " Working Cash Fund") and shall be used to pay the
general corporate expenses of the County in accordance with customary disbursement procedures of the
County.
Alternatively, the Chief Financial Officer may all ocate the proceeds of the Note to one or more other
funds or accounts of the County now in existence. The County by its Board reserves the right, as it
becomes necessary from time to time, to change the purposes of expend iture of the Working Cash Fund
or its accounts, to change priorities, to revise cost allocations between expenditures and to substitute
projects, in order to meet current needs of the County; subject, however, to the provisions of the tax
covenants of the County relating to the Tax Exem pt status of interest on the Note if it is issued as Tax
Exempt.

Section 2.7.

General Tax Covenants: In the event that the Note is issued as Tax Exempt, the
provisions of this Section shall apply. The County covenants that it will take no action with respect to the
proceeds of the Note which would result in making the interest payable on the Note subject to federal
income taxes by reason of the Note being classified as an "arbitrage bond" within the meaning of
Section 148 of the Code or rul ings or regulations promulgated thereunder.

349

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

The County also agrees and covenants with the purchaser and registered owner of the Note from time to
time outstanding that, to the extent possible under Ill inois law, it will comply with whatever federal tax
law is adopted in the future which app lies to the Note and affects the status of the interest on the Note as
Tax Exempt; that without limiting the generality of the foregoing, the County agrees: (a) through its
officers, to make such further specific covenants, representations and assurances as may be necessary or
advisable; (b) to comply with a ll representations, covenants and assurances contained in a certification
regarding tax exemption to be prepared by counsel approving the Note; (c) to consult with such counsel
and to comply with such advice as may be given; (d) to pay to the United States, as necessary, such sums
of money representing required rebates of excess arbitrage profits relating to the Note; (e) to fi le such
forms, statements and supporting documents as may be required and in a timely man ner; and (t) if
deemed necessary or advisable by its officers, to employ and pay fiscal agents, financial advisors,
attorneys and other persons to assist the County in such compliance; and that the County acknowledges
that, in the event of an examination by the Internal Revenue Service of the exemption from Federal
income taxation for interest paid on the Note, under present rules, the County is treated as the "taxpayer"
in such examination.

Section 2.8.
Registered Form: The County agrees that it will not take any action to permit the Note,
if it is issued as Tax Exempt, to be issued in, or converted into, bearer or coupon form.

06-R-287
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
REGARDING ANTICIPATED BUDGET SHORTFALL
IN THE COOK COUNTY BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVICES
WHEREAS, the budget of Cook County government is $3,046.7 million, and the specific budget for the
Bureau of Health Services is $950 million, representing approximately 32% of the total budget; and
WHEREAS, reports from the Office of the Comptroller and communications from the Bureau of Health
Services indicate a budget gap or shortfall of approximately $44 million; and
WHEREAS, testimony at various meetings of the Board and its Finance Committee, and correspondence
from Dr. Daniel H. Winship, Chief of the Bureau of Health Services, have been received by the Finance
Committee indicating the existence of this budget gap and a general plan for its reduction before the end
of the fiscal year on November 30, 2006; and
WHEREAS, it is of great concern to the President and Board of Commissioners, and in the public
interest of the people of Cook County, that the Bureau specify the measures and policies to be
implemented to reduce the budget shortfall and avoid a budget gap at the end of the fiscal year.

351

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services shall provide a detailed
plan for reducing the budget shortfall of $44 million in said agency before the end of the fiscal year on
November 30, 2006, and that such report be submitted to this Board no later than September I, 2006.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of Jul y 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

06-R-288
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CARL R. HANSEN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, the Chicago Harbor lock at 68 years old is I 8 years past its life expectancy, has eroded past
the point of repair, has required urgent large-scale repairs three times since 1992 to keep functioning, and
needs to be replaced; and
WHEREAS, the lock is a critical link in Ch icago's transportation system, opening and closing I I ,000
times a year to allow over 40,000 vessels to pass between Lake Michigan and the Chicago River, making
it the nation's second busiest lock; and
WHEREAS, recreational and commercial boating could be disrupted for weeks if the lock fails to open
or c lose properly, compromising the$ I 0 million annua l revenues from the tour boat industry; and
WHEREAS, the lock was built to help Illinois comply with the I930 U.S. Supreme Court decision that
strictly limits how much water the state can divert from Lake Michigan, and any sign ificant leakage at the
lock reduces the amount of lake water area communities can use to supply drinking water to growing
suburbs; and
WHEREAS, the lock is used as a mechan is m to prevent the river water from entering the lake in order to
manage pollutants, and is also a last resort safety valve that has been used five times since I 996 to keep
the Chicago River from overflowing its banks; and
WHEREAS, if the lock were to jam or experience outright failure at the wrong time it could prove
catastrophic for downtown Chicago, as in the case of the Loop Flood in I 992 whereby 250 million
gallons of water poured into downtown Chicago causing upward of$ I billion in damage; and
WHEREAS, the lock is owned by the Army Corps of Engineers, which stated in a I 999 study that
continuing to make repairs as needed is not a viable option; and
WHEREAS, new gates for the lock and machinery to operate them would cost nearly $20 million in
federal funding; and

352

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, members oflllinois' Congressional delegation have been working towards obtaining federal
funding for this crucial project, however, broad support is needed at the local, state and federal level to
make this federal financing a priority.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commi ssioners declares
that in order to promote and protect the safety and welfare of the citizens of Cook County, it is necessary
and in the best interest of the public that the C hicago Harbor lock be replaced; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County calls upon the
members of the United States House of Representatives and Senate, and upon the President of the United
States to fund the replacement of the Chicago Harbor lock as soon as possible.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE BOBBIE L. STEELE, EARLEAN COLLINS,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY
AND DEBORAH SIMS, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by

CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA AND MIKE QUIGLEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, a mammography is a special type of x-ray imaging used to create detailed images of the
breast; and
WHEREAS, the American Cancer Society estimates that in the year 2006, 212,292 women in the United
States will be diagnosed with breast cancer and 40,970 women will die of thi s devastating disease; and

353

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the American Cancer Society recommends that women age 40 and older have an annual
mammogram, annual clinical breast examination by a health care professional, and perform monthly
breast self-examinations; and

WHEREAS, there are approximately 11 ,000 women currently waiting to receive diagnostic breast health
services in the Cook County Bureau of Health Services System; and

WHEREAS, the Attorney General of the State of Illinois Lisa Madigan conducted a recent study on
charity care provided by non-profit hospitals. The study shows that twenty-one (21) Cook County notfor-protit hospital networks receive $326 million in property tax exemptions but provide $I 05 million in
charity care.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, due to the overwhelming demand to provide
mammography services throughout the Cook County Bureau of Health Services that the Cook County
Board of Commissioners hereby authorizes the Cook County Bureau of Health Services to establish a task
force which will include other health care providers, to explore the potential for property tax-exempt
hospitals to provide mammography services to women on the Bureau of Health Services waiting list as
part of the hospital 's charity care program; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the task force shall provide a report to the Cook County Board of
Commissioners by October I, 2006 with subsequent reports to follow o n a quarterly basis.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.

06-R-291
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN AND GREGG GOSLIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE J ERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
TO CALL A SPECIAL MEETING TO FILL VACANCY IN OFFICE OF PRESIDENT
WHEREAS, Cook County Board President, John H. Stroger, Jr. tendered a signed letter of resignation to
the Secretary of the Board and the Board of Commissioners on July 5, 2006; and

WHEREAS, Pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/2-6003 , "Vacancy in office of president," reads in pertinent part, as
follows:
In case of the ... resignation ...from office .. .of the president so elected ... If less than two
years and sixty days of the unexpired term remain, the board of commissioners shall elect
one of their number to serve the unexpired term of the president.

WHEREAS, President Stroger's resignation from the office of the President becomes effective on July
3 1, 2006, w ith approximately four months remai ning in his term as president; and

356

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the vacancy in the office of the President is as of August I , 2006; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Commissioner who is selected as the new president will need time for a
transition before taking office; and
WHEREAS, the public should be full y informed of the platform and qualifications of all board members
seeking to serve as President.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, THAT:
Pursuant to Rule 4-1 of the Rules of the Cook County Board of Commissioners, a Special Meeting of the
Board of Commissioners be called for Jul y .1.2., 2006 to select a member of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners to serve as President from August I, 2006 until December 4, 2006 (the unexpired term of
President Stroger) pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/2-6003 and that the public be given an opportunity to participate
in such meeting aeeording to the Board's Fl:lles in accordance with this Resolution.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that at any special meeting to elect a member to serve the unexpired
term of President, the President shall be elected by a simple majority of those present and voting on the
question; provided that a vote of "present" shall not be counted as voting on the question; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that at such special meeting, nominations shall be made from the floor
at the call of the Presiding Officer, which nominations shall not require a second; after nominations are
closed by the Presiding Officer, the nominees, in alphabetical order, shall be allowed ten minutes to speak
to the nomination; after which voting shall be by roll call pursuant to Chapter XIV of Robert's Rules of
Order, Newly Revised, 10th Edition, wherein each member when called upon shall declare his or her vote
for a single nominee or may vote " present;" the C lerk of the Board shall maintain a tally of the votes and
announce the tallv at the Presiding Officer' s direction; if, after a vote upon the nominations, a single
nom inee receives a simple majority of those present and voting on the question, the Presiding Officer
shall declare that member to have been elected President effective August I, 2006, upon taking the oath
of office, to serve until the newly elected President takes the oath of office on December 4, 2006; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that if. after a vote upon the nominations. a single nominee does not
receive a simple majority of those present and voting on the question, the Presiding Officer shall declare
no election and all previous nominations shall be cancelled; the Presiding Officer shall again call for
nominations from the floor, which nominations shall not require a second; after nominations are closed by
the Presiding Officer, the nominees who were not previouslv nominated shall be allowed ten minutes to
speak to the nomination, in alphabetical order; voting s hall again be by roll call pursuant to Chapter XIV
of Robert's Rules of Order, Newly Revised, 10th Edition, wherein each member when called upon shall
again declare his or her vote for a single nominee or may vote "present;" the C lerk of the Board shall
maintain a tally of the votes and announce the tally at the Presiding Officer's direction; this process shall
continue until a member receives a simple majority of those present and voting on the question; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that in order to accommodate the large number of persons who may
wish to express their views on thi s important matter. public participation shall be limited to written
testimony filed with the Secretary of the Board by July 18, 2006 so that it may be distributed to all Board
members.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DA YID ORR, County C lerk
