06-R-297
RESOLUTION
RESOLUTION TO ESTABLISH THE COOK COUNTY MEDICAL RESERVE CORPS
WHEREAS, the President of the United States created the Medical Reserve Corps (MRC) Program
under the auspices of the Surgeon General fo llowing the terrorist attacks of September 11 , 200 I in order
to coord inate volunteer activities of health professionals and others in preparing for and responding to
large scale emergencies such as an influenza epidemic, a natural disaster, or an act of terrorism; and
WHEREAS, the Medical Reserve Corps is a network of community-based, citizen volunteer Med ical
Reserve Corps Units, which provide health professionals and others an organized mechanism through
which they can vol unteer their time and skil ls to strengthen their communities by preparing for and
responding to large scale emergencies, as well as assisting their communities with ongoing public health
needs throughout the year, if desired; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County has established the Cook County Emergency
Services and Disaster Agency, also known as the Cook County Emergency Management Agency
(CCEMA), pursuant to the " Illinois Emergency Services and Disaster Act of 1975"; and

363

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners also serves as the Board of Health of Cook
County and has created the Cook County Department of Public Health (Department) to carry out public
health activities in the County; and
WHEREAS, the Department is the public health authority for Cook County, with the exception of
municipalities which operate health departments within Cook County which are certified by the Ill inois
Department of Public Health; and
WHEREAS, the CCEMA coordinates programs for disaster mitigation, preparedness, response and
recovery within the County in coordination with private organizations, political subdivisions, and the state
and federal governments; and
WHEREAS, the Department, in coordination with the CCEMA, engages in planning to prepare for
potential public health emergencies, including emergencies which may result in a declaration of disaster;
and
WHEREAS, in preparing to respond to a public hea lth emergency, the Department and the CCEMA
require that municipalities within Cook County assist in providing resources to help ensure that a
sufficient number of qualified personnel are available to engage in emergency response activities
including, but not limited to, personnel qualified to perform physical assessments, epidemiological
investigations, inoculations, medication dispensing, medication administration, minor medical treatments
and related and supportive activities; and
WHEREAS, the Department wishes to encourage munic ipalities to enlist volunteers within their
communities to engage in emergency response activities and the Department a lso wishes to enlist such
volunteers directl y; and
WHEREAS, the CCEMA may utilize and may administer oaths to volunteers who assist in performing
disaster mitigation, preparedness, response and recovery fu nctions within the County includi ng volunteer
health providers and others wis hing to j oin a Medical Reserve Corps unit to assist the Department and the
CCEMA in the event of a public health emergency; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners desires to establish the Cook County Medical
Reserve Corps to assist the Department and CCEMA in permitting volunteers identified by the
Department both directly and through municipalities to a id the Department and CCEMA during an
emergency that req uires additional personnel, particularly public health personnel and related and
supportive personnel.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Medical Reserve Corps is hereby
established for the purpose of recruiting and organ izi ng volunteers to assist the Department, the CCEMA
and the municipalities within Cook County to prepare fo r and respond to a public health emergency; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chief Operating Officer of the Cook County Department of
Public Health, subject to the approval and directions of the Director of the CCEMA, is hereby authori zed
to establish rules, policies, procedures and form agreements consistent with the provisions of applicable
law to faci litate the establishment and operation of a Cook County Medical Reserve Corps, which may
include munici pal chapters.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of Jul y 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

364

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called Alfred Edward Vaughn, Sr. from our
midst; and
WHEREAS, Alfred Edward Vaughn, Sr., the first born child of David Vaughn and Minnie Speaks
Vaughn, was born January 2, 19 I 0 in Postelle, Arkansas; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Vaughn maintained his farm in Postel le until he moved to Marvell, Arkansas in I 964.
He departed this life on Sunday, July 2, 2006; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Vaughn's chi ldhood education began at Hicks Elementary School and ended at Alcorn
A & M College in Lorman, Mississippi for High School. He also attended Shorter Junior College and A.
M. & N. College before receiving his Bachelors Degree from Philander Smith College; and
WHEREAS, Alfred was married to the late Blossie 8. Taylor on December 25, I 932. To their union
eight children were born. His wife, Blossie, and three sons, Leroy, Elmo and David, preceded him in
death; and
WHEREAS, known best by his students as Mr. Alfred, his profess ional experience consisted of 42 years
as a teacher and/or principal of Union (Frog Pond), McDade, Hicks, Postelle, Turner and Marvell
Elementary Schools. From the beginning of his marriage and until shortly before his retirement from
Marvell Elementary School in I 97 I , Mr. Vaughn enthus iastically operated a li vestock, cotton and corn
farm in Postelle; and
WHEREAS, although he was known for his quiet and reserved nature, he came to " life" when it was
time to fi sh, hunt and share family time. He is remembered for sharing sweet potatoes cooked under the
ashes of the fireplace, roasting peanuts, and making "snow" ice cream when the winter season permitted;
and
WHEREAS, with the passing of Alfred Edward Vaughn, Sr., we have lost not only a consummate
"fami ly man" and pillar of his community, but also a distinguished educator who made a positive impact
on the li ves of countless students. The myriad contributions Alfred Edward Vaughn, Sr. has made to our
world will forever resonate.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby express its deepest condolences and
most heartfelt sympathy to the family as well as the many friends and loved ones of Alfred Edward
Vaughn, Sr. ; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Alfred Edward Vaughn, Sr. so that his rich legacy may be so honored and ever cherished.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

CONGRATULATING THE ITALIAN NATIONAL SOCCER TEAM ON THEIR
CHAMPIONSHIP IN THE 2006 FIFA WORLD CUP
WHEREAS, the finals for the 2006 World Cup were completed on July 9, 2006, in Berlin, Germany; and
WHEREAS, hundreds of teams from around the world competed at various levels to qualify for the
World Cup in soccer; and
WHEREAS, thirty-two teams from six continents qualified to compete in the World Cup, with the
sixteen most victorious teams competing in the 2006 World Cup; and
WHEREAS, these teams represented their nations admirably, with great professionalism and skill in the
most played and watched sport in the world with estimates of over one billion people watching the final
game worldwide; and
WHEREAS, the Italian National Team was victorious in matches against Australia, Ukraine and
Germany in the tournament, eventually defeating the French National team in the final game; and
WHEREAS, the team consisted of Gianluigi Buffon, Angelo Peruzzi, Marco Amelia, Cristian Zaccardo,
Fabio Grosso, Fabio Cannavaro, Andrea Barzagli, Alessandro Nesta, Gianluca Zambrotta, Massimo
Oddo, Marco Materazzi, Daniele DeRossi, Gennaro Gattuso, Francesco Totti, Mauro Camoranesi,
Simone Barone, Simone Perrotta, Andrea Pirlo, Alessandro Del Piero, Luca Toni, Alberto Gilardino,
Vincenzo laquinta, and Filippo lnzaghi, and was coached by Marcello Lippi; and
WHEREAS, this 2006 victory represents the fourth World Cup championship for the Italian National
Team since the competition began in the early 1900s; and
WHEREAS, there are twenty five million Italian Americans in the United States of America, wi th over
five hundred thousand in the State of Illinois, and hundreds of thousands in the Cook County area; and
WHEREAS, soccer is a fast growing sport, with thousands of organizations and teams for children and
adults being organized in the City of Chicago and throughout the suburbs; and
WHEREAS, the Republic of Italy is a staunch ally and friend of the United States; and
WHEREAS, Italian Americans have contributed to the quality of life in a variety of fields, professions,
government, the arts and sciences.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Board of Commissioners of Cook
County, Illinoi s do hereby extend our congratulations and commendations to the Italian National Team
for their 2006 World Cup championship victory, extend our compliments to the people of Cook County of
Italian American heritage and to all soccer fans in our County, and extend our best wishes to the people of
Italy on this momentous occasion.
Approved and adopted this I 2th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

IN MEMORY OF REVEREND LARRY CRAIG
WHEREAS, Reverend Larry Craig passed away at the rectory of the Assumption of the Blessed Virgin
Mary Roman Catholic Church on June I 0, 2006 at the age of 59; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig devoted his life to embodying the biblical passage that reads, "whatever you do
for the least of my brothers, you do for me"; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig was a graduate of Quigley Preparatory Seminary, where he served as class
president, and the University of St. Mary of the Lake Seminary in Mundelein and was ordained in 1973;
and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig served at St. Sylvester parish from 1973 to 1978 and Providence of God from
1978 to 1984 before arriving at the Assumption of the Blessed Virgin Mary Roman Catholic Church,
delivering homilies in both English and Spanish; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig served as chaplain of the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center in
I 976, where he first became interested in assisting prisoners and their families; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig was asked by then Cardinal Joseph Bernardin what the archdiocese was missing,
he suggested a jail and juvenile detention ministry; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig founded Kolbe House in 1983 to minister to the needs of incarcerated people at
the Cook County Jail and Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center and based it at the
Assumption of the Blessed Virgin Mary Roman Catholic Church; and
WHEREAS, in 1980, Rev. Craig authored a prayer book to ease the fears of youth behind bars that is
still used in U.S. detention centers today ; and
WHEREAS, Rev. Craig is survived by his mother, Marie, two brothers, Tom and Bob, a sister, Sister
Mary Kathleen, and countless parishioners whose lives have been touched by his eloquence.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Rev. Larry
Craig and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of thi s Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the fami ly of Rev.
Larry Craig so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this I 2th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

37-46 record with the Wildcats, and becoming the second most winning football coach in school histoiy;
and

Wildcats to three postseason bowl games; and

perennial powerhouse Ohio State in Evanston since 1958 and the first to beat the Buckeyes since I971,
the first Northwestern head football coach to beat Penn State at Beaver Stadium, and enjoyed a 14-10
combined Big Ten record over the past three seasons; and

2000 Big Ten Conference Title one season after fini shing last in the Conference and was named the Dave
McClain Big Ten Coach of the Year and the Region 3 Coach of the Year by the American Football
Coaches Association (AFCA); and

four years for graduation rates of 100%; and

WHEREAS, Randy Walker's career coaching record of 96-81-5 ranks him 27th on the NCAA Division
I-A list of coaching victories for coaches with five or more years of I-A experience.

proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Randy

HONORING FATHER ROBERT "BOB" OLDERSHAW
WHEREAS, Father Robert " Bob" Oldershaw has retired from service at St. Nicholas' parish in Evanston
after 18 years; and

380

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, Father Bob has served as a priest for 44 years, first considering the priesthood in 4th grade
while at St. Mary's Parish School in Evanston, and continuing at Loyola Academy, Quigley Preparatory
Seminary and St. Mary of the Lake Seminary in Mundelein, becoming ordained in 1962; and
WHEREAS, Father Bob has been an inspiration to hi s parishioners and the entire community for his
dedication to human rights, social justice and community and world peace; and
WHEREAS, Father Bob has been a vocal supporter of immigrants rights and gun control; and
WHEREAS, since 1988, Father Bob has served as chaplain for the Police Department of Evanston; and
WHEREAS, Father Bob has been a respected community leader in his native community, s peaking at
City Council meetings, lobbyi ng in Springfield, participating in Leadership Evanston, the City's LongRange Planning Commi ssion, the Commi ssion on Panhandling, the AIDS Advisory Board and the Board
of Solidarity Bridge, as well as being an active member of the Evanston Ec umenical Action Commission
and the Evanston Interfaith Clergy, and is a fixture at many school-related meetings and community
functions; and
WHEREAS, in the aftennath of tragedy, when a former a ltar-boy murdered another young man, Father
Bob showed his parishioners and the world the healing power of faith when he brought the two fami lies
together and defined a priest's ability to bring love, compassion and tolerance to the toughest of times,
and in the course inspired the PBS documentary, A Justice That Heals, which has been shown throughout
the nation and world; and
WHEREAS, when, two years after becoming pastor of St. N icholas, the church opened its arms to
hundreds of Latino parishioners w hose church closed, Father Bob responded by traveling to Mexico twice
to immerse himself and learn Spanish well enough to preach and celebrate mass in that tongue; and
WHEREAS, under Fathe r Bob, St. N icholas celebrated the growi ng diversity of its parish by observing
the feast of Our Lady of Guadalupe for its Latino members, Sim bang Gabi, a Filipino pre-dawn mass said
for nine days prior to Christmas and the African-American hol iday of Kwanzaa, as well as hav ing a gay
and lesbian ministry, winning an award for the church's efforts to include those with physical and mental
challenges and establishing sharing paris hes in Haiti, Mexico and Chicago; and
WHEREAS, prior to coming to St. Nicholas, Father Bob served as assistant pastor at St. T homas the
Apostle parish in Hyde Park, at Holy Name Cathedral, and at St. C lements in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, in 1979, Father Bob served as liturgy coordinator of the mass in Grant Park during the visit
to Chicago of Pope John Paul II ; and
WHEREAS, Father Bob has always demonstrated a love for the music ministry, forming a gi rl 's bell
choir at the Cathedral and forming a youth choir at St. Thomas that perfo nned church and secular music,
including a production of Fiddler on the Roof that went on a tour that included synagogues and rest
homes; and
WHEREAS, Father Bob will spend six months on sabbatical in Italy and the Middle East and intends to
return to St. Nicholas as pastor emeritus to continue such services as officiating weddings and providing
comfort to griev ing parishioners; and
WHEREAS, Cook County owes a debt of gratitude to Father Bob for his inspiring and successful
ministry, public service and leadership.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Father Robert " Bob" Oldershaw on his 44 year ministry and wishes him happiness,
good health, and success in his impressive future endeavor; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Father Bob as a
symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.

COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF DAVID DOTY
WHEREAS, David Doty passed away at his home in Western Springs on Tuesday, June 27, 2006 at the
age of6 1; and
WHEREAS, David Doty is survived by Diane, his wife of over 35 years, his two sons, Jeffery and
Michael, his daughter Erin, two grandchi ldren and many nieces and nephews; and

382

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 12, 2006

WHEREAS, David Doty was involved with public poli cy and the political system through both his work
as vice president of state government affairs at AT&T and as committeeman of the Republican party of
Lyons Township and as Treasurer of the Cook County Republican Central Committee; and
WHEREAS, in a career that spanned four decades, David Doty helped shape and direct
telecommunications public policy through the breakup of Ma Bell, the deregulation of 1996 and the
advent of the Internet and broadband; and
WHE REAS, David Doty began working in the telecommunications field in 1970 when he took a position
in the public relations department of the former Western Electric Hawthorne Works in Cicero; and
WHEREAS, David Doty represented AT&T before the state legislatures and regulatory commissions in
Illinois, Indiana, Michigan, Ohio, and Wisconsin, as wel l as on the national stage during the 1996 federal
telecommunications deregulation bill; and
WHEREAS, David Doty was a very effective advocate in Springfield, who was widely respected by all
who knew him and uni versally liked on both sides of the aisle, and whose loss will be felt by policy
makers throughout the Midwest; and
WHEREAS, David Doty brightened the lives of everyone he touched, and his infectious, hearty laugh
caused co-workers to go out of their way to sneakily plant jokes or cartoons at David's desk to start an
infectious ripple that spread throughout the office; and
WHEREAS, in addition to public policy, David Doty was also very committed to a full spiritual life,
bringing peace and justice to all he encountered; and
WHEREAS, David Doty will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew hi m and the
people of Cook County owe a debt of gratitude to David Doty for his civic involvement.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the fami ly and friends of David Doty
and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a s uitable copy of th is Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the fami ly of David
Doty so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of Ju ly 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commiss ioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE GREGG GOSLIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, CARL R. HANSEN,
MIKE QUIGLEY AND PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
INCREASE COUNTY FEES TO ADJUST FOR INFLATION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board passed Budget Amendment No. 56 during the FY 2004 budget
session; and
WHEREAS, the amendment called for the County to increase fees to adjust fo r inflation (cost of living)
and current rates at other local governments per the recommendations of a 200 I fee study generated by
the Chief Administrative Officer; and
WHEREAS, the amendment called for an increase in fees from the following departments: Recorder of
Deeds, County Clerk, Animal Control, Environmental Control, Building and Zoning, Revenue, Public
Administrator, Liquor Control, Medica l Examiner and supportive services th rough Public Safety/Judicial
Coordination; and
WHEREAS, to date, many of these fees have not been raised as directed by the Cook County Board.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby direct the Chief Administrative Officer to report to the Board by September 7th which fees have
been raised and when; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Chief Administrative Officer also recalculate the proposed fee
increases to adjust for inflation in 2006 and similar fees and rates currently charged at other local
governments.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
A ITEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

MIKE QUIGLEY AND PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
PLAN TO CONSOLIDATE BUREAU OF HEALTH DEPARTMENTS
AUTHORIZED BY FY 2005 BUDGET AMENDMENT NO. 9
WHEREAS, FY 2005 Budget Amendment No. 9 was approved by the Board of Commissioners as part
of the FY 2005 budget; and
WHEREAS, FY 2005 Budget Amendment No. 9 called for the consolidation of all separate and
duplicative departments within the Bureau of Health Services such as: Finance, Human Resources, Public
Affairs and Public Safety into a newly created Bureau of Health Admini stration within the Bureau of
Health Services by the fourth fi scal quarter of FY 2005 ; and
WHEREAS, said consol idation was projected to achieve an annualized cost savings of $8,403, 195 with a
fourth quarter savings of$2,403, 195; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services is $43,99 1,000 behind revenue projections through the
second quarter of FY 2006.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that by August I, 2006 the Bureau of Health Services wi ll
present its plan to meet the consolidation mandates outlined in FY 2005 Amendment No. 9 together with
a timetable to achieve said consolidations.
Approved and adopted this 12th day of July 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATIEST: DAVID ORR, County C lerk

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Comm issioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

ELIMINATIN G DUPLICATIVE PERSONNEL
WHEREAS, at the Board Meeting of June 20, 2006 the Board approved several contracts for the Bureau
of Health Services to outsource billing and collections; and
WH EREAS, the Board approved Item #57, a contract with Eligibility Services, Inc. to provide
Prescription C la ims Processing Services fo r the Bureau of Hea lth Services institutions; and
WHEREAS, the Board approved Item #58, a contract with Chamberlin Edmonds, to attempt collections
of Socia l Security Income/Social Security Disability Income fo r applications denied by Medicaid; and
WHEREAS, the Board also approved Item #59, a contract with NE BO, to provide Retroacti ve Claims
Processing Services for the Bureau of Health Services institutions to reprocess outpatient accounts to
identi fy additional third party revenue; and
WHEREAS, the Bureau of Health Services representatives stated that these contracts would free up
fi nance personnel from similar duties.
NOW, T HEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services will eliminate those
positions in the finance department responsible fo r perfo rming these contracted services, mak ing these
positions unnecessary; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Bureau of Health Services will present a plan by A ugust I,
2006 to identify and eliminate these unnecessary positions.
Approved and adopted thi s 12th day of Jul y 2006.
JO HN H. STROGER, JR ., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATT EST: DAVID ORR, County C lerk

may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

adopted. The motion carried.

Commissioners Butler and Maldonado voted "no".
